Disciplinary Action for Personnel of the National Government Flood Relief Committee 140

Song Ziwen and Zha Liangzhao Send Letters Requesting Reconsideration

The impeachment case in Anhui Province, which caused a national sensation last year, by the Control Yuan, after multiple investigations by the Central Government Disciplinary Committee, drafted a resolution proving that the impeachment was false, clearing the names of the impeached individuals, Vice Chairman of the Flood Relief Committee Xin Puson, Director of the Urgent Relief Office Zha Liangzhao, Anhui Relief Commissioner Quan Shaowu, Bengbu Grain Station Director Deruizhi, and Transportation Commissioner Yang Shucheng, confirming that they were innocent and had not committed any malfeasance. This has been reported in newspapers. Although the Disciplinary Committee exempted Xin Puson and Deruizhi from disciplinary action, it also separately imposed reprimands and demerits on the remaining three individuals outside of the case details. The punished individuals believe that they have been wronged. Even if the accusers are not punished in return, why should they be punished outside of the case details? Moreover, based on the facts, this punishment is not deserved. This case concerns the future of disaster relief and the credibility and reputation of the Flood Relief Committee. If it is not corrected, enthusiastic individuals will view social relief as a daunting task. Therefore, they visited Song Ziwen, Chairman of the National Government Flood Relief Committee, requesting that he send letters to the Judicial Yuan and the Central Government Disciplinary Committee based on the facts, requesting a swift reconsideration of the proposed disciplinary actions, so as to clarify right and wrong and encourage action. Mr. Zha Liangzhao also sent an express telegram to the Disciplinary Committee. The original texts of the letters and telegrams have been found and are recorded below to clarify the truth.

Letter from the National Government Relief Committee for Flood Disasters 141

To the esteemed National Government's Judicial Yuan and the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee:

We hereby inform you that, according to the reports submitted by Cha Liangzhao, former Director of the Emergency Relief Office of this Committee, Quan Shaowu, former Commissioner of Relief Affairs in Northern Anhui, and Yang Shucheng, former Transportation Commissioner, regarding the impeachment case concerning relief affairs in Northern Anhui, which resulted in penalties of admonition and demerit recording, we request that these reports be forwarded to the Judicial Yuan and the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee for a swift review of the disciplinary actions in this case. We enclose copies of the original reports for your consideration.

Respectfully,

National Government Relief Committee for Flood Disasters

Enclosure: Original Reports

"Respectful Greetings to Chairman Song:

We have received the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee's order of February 16th, along with document Jian Zi No. 122, regarding the resolution of the impeachment case concerning relief affairs in Northern Anhui. The Committee, based on its investigation of the facts, has proven that the charges brought by Supervisory Committee Member Gao Yihan and others regarding (1) price changes, (2) short weights, (3) flour conversion, and (4) delays, were without any evidence of personal gain or corruption. Those subjected to disciplinary action should not be held responsible. For years, we have endured unjust accusations and suffering, which can now be alleviated.

However, unexpectedly, beyond the scope of the case, we were given the punishments of admonition and demerit recording. The Committee may have other intentions, but the matter is extremely perplexing, and we feel wronged. Therefore, we must address the facts. The Committee resolved that, because Liangzhao, as the Director of the Emergency Relief Office, did not request that the sale of Bengbu wheat be waived due to the special circumstances in Northern Anhui, he was penalized with "one demerit recording". According to the facts, the price change of relief wheat was an integral part of the Water Disaster Relief Committee's overall plan to meet the needs of relief work, and Liangzhao had also contributed his opinions regarding the price change of Bengbu wheat. Therefore, Bei Ke, the Director of the Joint Storage Office, stated in his official letter explaining the reasons for the Bengbu price change, "The Joint Storage Office and the Emergency Relief Office strongly opposed it, fearing that the relief grain would not arrive and the food of the disaster victims would be at risk." (This letter is attached to this Committee's reply No. 396 to the Committee). Moreover, the Bengbu wheat sold at that time was intended for the urgent needs of the joint construction and emergency relief in the district. In terms of responsibilities, the Emergency Relief Office was not in a position to interfere, nor did it have any responsibility to bear.

Furthermore, the Committee resolved that Shaowu's "dereliction of duty" was due to his "being headstrong," and he was penalized with a "written admonition". According to the facts, this Committee, in order to promote relief affairs in Northern Anhui, established a separate special zone and sent Shaowu to cooperate with Chinese and Western relief organizations to actively implement relief. Within six weeks, the emergency relief work in Northern Anhui was completed expeditiously. Because he was loyal to his duty, he was subjected to jealousy and impeachment, and suffered the slander of being "headstrong". Those who falsely accused him were unable to achieve their aims, and intensified their efforts, fabricating various rumors and inverting right and wrong. This is why the Supervisory Yuan had the impeachment case concerning relief affairs in Northern Anhui, and the Anhui native association in Shanghai had the false accusation in the Shanghai court. Now, the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee has taken this as evidence of dereliction of duty and given him an admonition. Considering the facts, how can this be considered fair?

The Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee stated that Shucheng "only knew about private interests and not public interests," and was penalized with "two demerit recordings". According to the facts, Shucheng witnessed the suffering of the people affected by the disaster in Henan and Anhui, so he responded to the invitation of the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters while he was very busy with business, and asked to assist in the relief transportation. Before and after the January 28th Incident, he personally provided funds to fly to Shanghai, Hankou, and Zhengzhou to contact relief transportation vehicles for the Disaster Relief Committee. He obtained the consent of He Jingwu, Director of the Pinghan Railway, and Qian Zongze, Director of the Longhai Railway, to have the coal and troop transport vehicles heading to Pukou carry relief wheat on their return trips. At that time, Shucheng also sacrificed his personal business and personally stationed in Pukou to assist Yu Shaojun, the director of the grain station, in taking care of the relief wheat transportation for more than thirty days. Even those who were asked to assist with enthusiasm were purely voluntary and did not receive any remuneration from the Disaster Relief Committee. Furthermore, because the Shanghai War affected the sale of American wheat by the Disaster Relief Committee in Shanghai, Shucheng's Baoxing Flour Mill was consulted, and, in the interest of disaster relief, agreed to sell a portion of the American wheat on its behalf. The price offered was higher than the prices offered by other factories in Shanghai and the factory's own purchase price of Australian wheat. This can be verified by the financial records of the Disaster Relief Committee. Unexpectedly, those who falsely accused him claimed that Shucheng was profiting from it, and falsely accused Shucheng of delaying relief transportation. Therefore, we had to earnestly defend against the false accusations. Now, the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee said that Shucheng constantly debated, and identified him as "only knowing about private interests and not public interests," and gave him a demerit recording punishment. For the sake of right and wrong and for the sake of those who are enthusiastic about helping with relief in the future, Shucheng must state the facts in detail to defend himself.

In summary, the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee, outside of the original impeachment case, imposed penalties of admonition and demerit recording on us, which are not deserved. How can we be willing to accept them? Furthermore, it concerns the entire honor of the National Government Relief Committee for Flood Disasters. Therefore, we earnestly appeal to the Chairman to forward our request to the Judicial Yuan and the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee for a swift review of the disciplinary actions in this case, in order to clarify right and wrong and to manifest justice.

Cha Liangzhao, former Director of the Emergency Relief Office

Quan Shaowu, former Commissioner of Relief Affairs in Northern Anhui

Yang Shucheng, former Transportation Commissioner

Respectfully,

Jiang, March 3rd"

Cha Liangzhao's Express Mail Telegram 142

"To the esteemed Chairman Tan and members of the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee in Nanjing:

I respectfully telegram requesting a review of the disciplinary actions in the Northern Anhui relief impeachment case, in order to clarify right and wrong and to manifest justice. I have received the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters' forwarding of your Committee's order of February 16th and the resolution regarding the Northern Anhui relief impeachment case. After reading them, I am extremely perplexed. In the autumn of the 21st year of the Republic, Supervisory Committee Member Gao Yihan and others picked up rumors, disregarded the facts, and filed an impeachment case based on unfounded charges of "personal gain and corruption", falsely accusing Deputy Chairman Simpson of this Committee and Liangzhao and other colleagues handling relief affairs in Northern Anhui. Fortunately, your Committee has spent more than a year investigating in many ways, and has proven with facts that the allegations in the original impeachment case regarding the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters' price changes and flour conversion, etc., were without any evidence of corruption or error, and that the impeachers should not be held responsible in any way. We were hoping that your Committee would reveal the truth of this relief impeachment case, which has attracted national attention, and that the unjust accusations and suffering that we have endured for years would be alleviated. However, unexpectedly, your Committee has suddenly made arbitrary judgments about the handling of the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters' affairs at the time, and penalized Liangzhao with "one demerit recording". Considering the facts, the penalty is not deserved, and judging by the regulations, I dare not fail to defend myself. The reason for the disciplinary action given by your Committee's resolution is that Liangzhao "as the Director of the Emergency Relief Office, did not request that the sale of Bengbu wheat be waived due to the special circumstances in Northern Anhui." However, the attachment to the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters' reply No. 396 cited in your Committee's resolution (the official letter from Yun Ke, Director of the Transportation and Storage Office, regarding the price change of Bengbu relief wheat in May of the 21st year of the Republic) clearly states, "The Joint Construction Office and the Joint Relief Office strongly opposed it, fearing that the relief grain would not arrive and the food of the disaster victims would be at risk." This means that Liangzhao did contribute the above opinions regarding the measures taken by the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters at that time to meet the needs of relief work. Moreover, the Bengbu wheat that was sold by the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters during the Shanghai War was purely intended to meet the urgent needs of joint construction and relief in the Huai District, and had nothing to do with the Emergency Relief Office. Furthermore, your Committee's resolution also recognized that "the price change of relief wheat by the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters was part of the overall plan of the entire relief fleet to cope with the environment," and that "the cash sale of Bengbu wheat was a last resort at the time (due to the impact of the January 28th Shanghai War)". Liangzhao, as the Director of the Emergency Relief Office, could not be held "responsible" for it. As a member of the social service community, and for the sake of the Relief Committee for Flood Disasters' reputation, I dare not fail to state my views directly. Your Committee is clearly discerning and will surely make factual corrections to clarify right and wrong, so that society has a standard to follow, and the general public will not regard social relief work as a perilous path. This would be fortunate. I send this urgent telegram and await your orders with utmost anticipation. Cha Liangzhao, former Director of the Emergency Relief Office of the National Government Relief Committee for Flood Disasters

Respectfully,

Yang, (March 7th)"

Conflict Between Wu Song Customs Brokers and Ship Registration Office 148

Registration Procedures are Slow

Causing a Misunderstanding

A conflict occurred due to the detention of ship merchants by patrol officers from the Wusong Ship Donation Registration Office of the Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau. The details are as follows:

Reason for Occurrence 149

On the eighth of this month, the Ningbo fishing boat "Jin Wanxing" came to Song from Yong loaded with aquatic products and fish for sale. It was immediately reported to the Xieji Customs Broker, which sent Lin Yinsheng to the Wusong Ship Registration Office of the Public Works Bureau to report the registration. However, the registration license was not obtained due to procedural matters. Unexpectedly, on the same day, a patrol boat from the Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau discovered that the "Jin Wanxing" had not registered and intended to conceal the donation and evade taxes. A fine of forty yuan was imposed. The shipowner felt unfairly penalized and refused to accept it. Patrol officers then confiscated the boat's gear, canopy, and sampan. After Xieji learned of this, the plaintiff Lin Yinsheng filed a statement with the Registration Office, but was detained and sent to Shanghai until the evening, when he was released. This aroused the indignation of all Wusong customs brokers. On one hand, they filed a written complaint with the Shanghai Fisheries Association, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Wusong Branch Office, which was forwarded to the Municipal Government, requesting that someone be sent to investigate. On the other hand, they planned to convene a meeting of all customs brokers to discuss countermeasures.

Letter to the Fisheries Association 150

To the esteemed Fisheries Association:

Our company's "Jin Wanxing" merchant ship arrived in Song with aquatic products and fish at approximately 8:00 AM on the eighth of this month. Our company handled customs clearance and ship donation registration matters, and opened up the names of the shipowners and ship masters, and the location of the ship docking was reported to the Wusong Office of the Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau ship affairs office to check for registration. Unexpectedly, at around 2:00 PM, the ship affairs office inspection boat came to Song and inspected the "Jin Wanxing" ship, and falsely accused the "Wanxing" ship of concealing the donation and evading taxes, and imposed a fine of forty yuan. The shipowners were unfairly penalized and could not bear it, and requested that our company send someone to explain to avoid being innocent. Our company sent an employee, Lin Yinsheng, together with the shipowner, to explain and prove and request a re-examination to avoid punishment. Unexpectedly, the inspectors Wang Chunsheng, etc., were unreasonable and not only did not accept our company's explanation, but also severely beat our employee Lin Yinsheng, and then arbitrarily detained him in the ship, imprisoned him in the cabin, sent him to Shanghai, forced him to sign a document, and detained him for more than six hours before releasing him. Tax donations are originally the obligations of the people. Now that the shipowner has already reported the application, it is not illegal or unreasonable. The inspector's order for extra punishment is inappropriate. Our company's sending of staff to provide proof and request a re-examination is also a proper procedure. Now, it has been unjustly insulted and detained. Not only has our company suffered injustice, but the shipowners will be unimaginable in the future. This letter is to the esteemed Fisheries Association, which will forward it to the Shanghai Municipal Government, requesting that officials be sent to investigate and remove from office to uphold justice and extend the humiliation.

Respectfully,

Wusong Xieji Business Firm, Manager Yang Qijue

Wu Jianguang Accuses His In-Laws 153

Even Wu's Own Daughter-in-Law is Among Those Accused

As a Result, the Daughter-in-Law's Part is Rejected and the Rest Will be Summoned Again

"It Started Because of Demanding Overdue Debts, Holding Grudges, and Coming to Make Trouble"

Wu Jianguang, who is blind, is originally from Meixian, Guangdong. He is seventy years old and has been running a fortune-telling shop at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Zhili Road for decades. His son, Zhongliang, married Wu Huang, the second daughter of Huang Fuji, who is also from the same hometown. Last year, Wu Jianguang's wife, Wu Li, suddenly sued Huang Fuji's eldest daughter, Liang Huang, and Liang Huang's husband, Liang Yishan, in the Civil Division of the First Special Court for failing to repay a debt of one thousand yuan. The court ruled in favor of the plaintiff and the Liangs lost the case. When it came to the execution of the judgment, the Liangs still refused to comply. The court issued an arrest warrant and arrested Liang Huang. After paying bail, she held a grudge and went to Wu's place to make trouble. Therefore, Wu Jianguang hired lawyer Xi Yafu to file a criminal complaint with the First Special Court, accusing his in-laws Huang Fuji, Huang's wife Zhong, Huang's son Peichu, eldest daughter Liang Huang, and second daughter Wu Huang, of offenses such as damaging property, theft, and insult. He also attached a private prosecution, requesting that the defendants be jointly and severally ordered to compensate the plaintiff for a fortune-telling tool and a loss of ten yuan. The content of the lawsuit stated that at approximately 6:00 PM on January 31st of this year, the defendants held a grudge and came to the plaintiff's home to make trouble. Without asking the reason, they cursed loudly, calling the plaintiff's daughter Wu Xiufeng a prostitute (note that Wu Xiufeng had a marriage dispute with Lu Xifan), and accusing the plaintiff of setting up a fortune-telling shop to make money and deserving to be kidnapped. They smashed all the teapots and teacups in the plaintiff's shop. A mahogany chair that the plaintiff was sitting on was also damaged, and the plaintiff's fortune-telling tool of more than fifty years was also stolen. The patrol officers from the Laozha Police Station arrived and went to the police station together. Later, because they were relatives, they did not pursue the matter further. However, the defendants' actions violated Articles 325 of the Criminal Law regarding defamation, Article 337 regarding theft, and Article 382 regarding damage to property.

Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Xiangzu presided over the hearing of this case in the Fifth Criminal Division. All the defendants were present and hired lawyer Jiang Chiping to defend them. The plaintiff Wu Jianguang immediately claimed that because my wife previously accused Liang Huang and others of owing money, and the court issued an arrest warrant and bailed them out, the defendants came to make trouble and fight at 6:00 PM on January 31st. Among them, the defendant Huang Zhong was the most ferocious, accusing me of swindling money and kidnapping, and calling my daughter a prostitute. The most hateful thing was that they stole my fortune-telling tool, which I have needed every day for fifty years, making it impossible for me to eat. As for their insulting words, if I wanted to tell them all, it would take several hours, and I don't want to say more now. He then presented the teapots, etc., as evidence. The defendants were questioned,

They all denied fighting and destroying property. Judge Wu reviewed the confessions and evidence, stating that the case still required further investigation, and ordered a postponement until the 22nd of this month for another hearing. He also advised both parties' lawyers to try to reach a settlement during the postponement, and if the settlement failed, the trial would proceed. Huang Wu, because she is the plaintiff's daughter-in-law, cannot be sued according to law, so the rejection was declared.

Double-Decker Buses Scheduled to Begin on the 20th 162

Each Vehicle Costs 30,000 Yuan

According to the Huadong News Agency, the Public Omnibus Company of the Public Concession has contracted with England to build forty double-decker buses, including all machinery, chassis, and other components. One vehicle has already arrived in Shanghai. The company has completed assembly in Shanghai and has begun test runs, which have proven to be very stable. According to investigations by the Huadong News Agency reporter at the company, the double-decker buses are scheduled to officially begin operations on the 20th of this month. However, due to the height of the bus, some overhead power lines along the route are too low and obstruct its operation. The Concession Tram Company is currently working to modify these lines. If the modifications can be completed before the 20th, the buses will definitely begin operations on that date. Otherwise, there may be a slight delay. These double-decker buses have 34 horsepower. The lower level can carry 40 passengers, and the upper level can carry 34 passengers. The entire body is made of steel and produced by the British Tilling Stevens factory. Due to the high price of the buses, the engine is a German diesel engine. After operations begin, the initial route will be Route 1, from Zhaofeng Garden to the Park Shooting Range, passing through Yidingpan Road, Jing'an Temple Road, Seymour Road, Tongfu Road, Mahuo Road, New World, Ballgame Field, the Bund on Nanjing Road, Tiantong Road, the Shooting Range, the Japanese School, and Shigaota Road. The fare for the lower level will remain the same, while the fare for the upper level will be higher, but the maximum increase will be no more than four copper coins. The first stop will cost eight copper coins, two stops twelve, three stops sixteen, four stops twenty, and five stops twenty-two. Subsequently, each additional stop will cost two copper coins, up to a maximum of forty coins. The ticket format for the upper and lower levels will be the same, but the upper-level tickets will have the letters "U.S.A." added. In the future, there will be two conductors assigned to each bus for the upper and lower levels. Children under the age of five will ride for free. It is said that the cost of each bus is approximately 30,000 Chinese yuan. (The above picture is a photograph of the double-decker bus.)

Railway Bureau Preparing Small Gardens at Various Stations 163

The Railway Bureau plans to develop small gardens along the major stations of the two railways. The Railway Bureau has previously issued orders to the Traffic Department to make preparations. At the same time, it ordered the Property Section of the General Affairs Department to send personnel to coordinate the matter. The section has now agreed on the procedures with the General Affairs Section of the Traffic Department. First, the engineering and traffic departments will instruct their respective sections to survey suitable locations at each major station, create drawings, and submit them to the Property Section for review. If the land is leased, it will be reclaimed from the tenants. The Engineering Department will prepare a plan and cost estimate for the arrangement of the garden and submit it to the bureau for approval. The purchase of flowers and trees will either be sourced from the Ningbo section or prepared by the Jiaxing nursery. The Property Section will consult with the nursery after the locations have been determined. The first steps are currently underway.

Suicide Case of a Young Woman Occurs 164

Mother-in-Law Seeks Justice for Daughter-in-Law; Thug Flees Guiltily

Ultimately, Justice Prevails; Questioning Official Respects Humanity

Sun Genfa, 26 years old, a local, lives in Tanjiacai, Zhabei. He owns several tiled houses. Besides his own residence, the remaining houses are rented out to others. He lives with his elderly mother, surnamed Shao, who is 52 years old, and his wife, surnamed Li, who is 26 years old. Recently, Genfa has been away on car business, leaving his mother and wife alone at home. Unexpectedly, a tenant named Wang Dechang, seeing that Genfa was often away and that his mother and wife were both women who could be bullied, frequently harassed Li. Being a traditional woman, she was well-mannered and sternly refused. Wang, shamed into anger, took advantage of Shao's absence on the afternoon of the 28th of last month at about 6 p.m., when Li had just returned to her bedroom after collecting rent from another tenant, Zhou Zhengyu. Wang broke into Li's bedroom and used barbaric means to force himself upon her. Li, feeling humiliated, cried for help. Nearby neighbors gathered to watch. Wang, enraged, beat Li severely, causing her body to be covered in injuries. Afterward, he used vile language to humiliate Li. After suffering this humiliation, she felt depressed and secretly purchased raw opium to ingest in an attempt to kill herself. When discovered, she was sent to the Renji Hospital in the Concession for treatment, but she died at around 4 a.m. on the 31st. Her family took custody of the body for burial. Wang Dechang, feeling guilty after Li's death, moved all his belongings to another location in an attempt to escape. Yesterday, the deceased's aunt, along with the deceased's mother, Li Gao, and witnesses Wu Gongquan and Zhao Ruyao, went to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau to seek justice. District Chief Lai dispatched police officers to arrest Wang Dechang. District Chief Zheng Zuhan interrogated Sun Shao, who recounted the events. Li Gao stated that she was 68 years old, from Gaojiaxiang, Pudong, and that the deceased was her daughter. She was informed by Shao, but when she arrived, her daughter had already died. Both women pleaded for justice. Witness Wu Gongquan stated that he was 24 years old, from Suzhou, and lived at 1557 Zhongxing Road. That evening, he happened to pass by the area and saw a crowd gathered. Li was crying loudly. He heard from the crowd that Li had been beaten for rejecting Wang's harassment. Zhao Ruyao stated that he was 30 years old, from Shanghai, and worked as a postal worker living at 82 Huakang Road. He learned that the above situation was true when he was delivering mail. Wang Dechang stated that he was 50 years old, from Anhui, and lived at 2 Tanjiacai and ran a weaving factory. He denied harassing Li and did not admit to beating the deceased. The interrogating official stated that since multiple people had testified that Wang Dechang had beaten Li, resulting in her death, it was a major homicide case and should be sent to the Public Security Bureau for thorough investigation in order to uphold humanity.

Victim of Prostitute Murder Case Autopsy Yesterday Reveals Death by Poisoning Then Stabbing 165

Strange Sounds Heard In The Deceased's Room

Security Guard Terrified, Sets Off Firecrackers All Night For Reassurance

In the Chizhi brothel opened by Yangzhou native Wang Fushou at No. 15 Hengmaoli, Mintini Yin Road, French Concession, 18-year-old Yangzhou prostitute Wang Guixiang accompanied Tianjin customer surnamed Wang to sleep in the front room on the third floor of the brothel on the evening of the 11th. Around 9 a.m. the following morning, it was discovered that the prostitute had been stabbed to death and the customer surnamed Wang had also sustained severe stab wounds. Upon receiving the report, the French Police dispatched detectives to investigate. No murder weapon was found in the room. Because the customer surnamed Wang had serious injuries and was unable to speak, the truth was difficult to ascertain. The customer was transported to Guangci Hospital for treatment. At the same time, the prostitute's body was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Mortuary to await an autopsy. Details of the matter were previously published in this newspaper yesterday. Yesterday morning, the Second Special District District Court Prosecutor's Office received a report from the Police and commissioned Prosecutor Wang, along with forensic doctor Wei Ligong and clerk Peng Xiang, to visit the mortuary at 11:00 a.m. to conduct an autopsy. The deceased's body was wrapped in a cotton quilt, wearing a striped white flannel shirt and trousers, a rose-red crepe silk short cotton jacket, and a gray worsted cotton jacket. She had unbound feet, wearing silk stockings, without shoes. Her hair had been cut off, and her face was completely purple-black. Her eyes were tightly closed, and the tip of her tongue was slightly protruding from her mouth. Blood foam was flowing from her mouth and nose. The buttons on her chest were unbuttoned. There was a forceful wound in the center of the sternum, about the size of a broad bean, about three inches deep. There were no bloodstains on her chest, only on the bed sheet. There were several clumps of bloodstains flowing from her mouth and nose. After a detailed examination of the external appearance by the forensic doctor, it appeared that she had been poisoned first and then stabbed to death. In order to clarify the true cause of death, the clothing worn by the deceased was removed. The chest was dissected, and two sloping knife holes were found on the stomach. The knife head had been inserted slightly, and then withdrawn slightly, without leaving the wound, before being inserted again diagonally. The blood in the stomach was examined again, and it was confirmed that she had been poisoned before being stabbed to death. Half a teacup of liquid was extracted for the police to test. The examination lasted for an hour before it was completed. The judge took his seat and first heard the report from Detective Zhang Chunsheng on the results of the investigation. Prostitute servant Zhu Dengfu testified that he was sleeping on a small shelf when he heard the customer surnamed Wang running from upstairs to the half-stairway, shouting "Someone, someone." He went out to look and saw Wang standing on the staircase. He called out to the owner to check the front and back doors downstairs first, which were locked. When he returned to the third floor, he saw Wang sitting on the bed, also wounded and bleeding. Miss Guixiang was already dead on the bed. He did not know how the two of them were injured or killed. Brothel madam Wang Zhang testified that she heard Zhu Dengfu shouting and went out to look and saw Wang standing on the staircase, wearing a short coat. When Wang returned to the room, they went up and saw Wang sitting by the bed, also with a knife wound on his chest, bleeding. Guixiang was already dead on the bed. Being a young woman, she was terrified. The old man was involved in a lawsuit, and there was no one at home, so she ordered the maidservant Wang Fang to report to the patrolmen, etc. However, no family members of the deceased came forward, and the brothel was unwilling to claim the body. The court ruled that Wang Guixiang died from poisoning and stabbing. The body was photographed and buried by the Tongren Fuyuan Hall. The police department was ordered to arrest the perpetrator and bring them to justice. It was also reported that after the case occurred, the brothel madam and servants were too frightened to stay in the house, leaving it empty. At night, patrol officers were dispatched by the police to guard the house until late at night, and they heard strange sounds from upstairs. The patrolman was also alarmed and reported to the head patrolman, who dispatched several more patrolmen to guard the house and set off firecrackers to provide reassurance all night, but no sounds were heard. This was also a miracle.

Dancer Vanishes Without a Trace, Lover Commits Suicide by Hanging 166

Discovered Three Days After Hanging

The Scene Can Be Described as Tragic

Chen Meiyu, also known as Huiying, a dancer from Ningbo at the Xinxin Dance Hall on Guizhou Road, was twenty-three years old. She was quite attractive and known for her romantic nature. Several years ago, she met Tang Guanlin (twenty-seven years old), a neighbor from Pudong. After that, the two communicated their affections and met in secret, like inseparable lovers. Last year, they rented a house together at No. 1257 Siwenli, Datong Road, and lived together. However, Tang had been unemployed recently, so Chen was entirely responsible for their livelihood through her performance. Over the past year, Chen began to feel disdain for Tang's lack of employment and started to seek pleasure elsewhere. One evening, she did not return home all night. When she returned home the next day, Tang asked where she had been. She claimed to have stayed at a sister's place. Because of this, the two argued and quarreled. Chen left in anger and never returned. Tang became increasingly resentful and despaired of life. He locked himself in the bedroom and committed suicide by hanging. It wasn't until the day before yesterday when Li, the second landlord, noticed that there was no sound coming from the room and the door was still locked. She became suspicious and peeked through the crack in the door, where she caught a glimpse of Tang already hanging. He had been dead for three or four days. She immediately reported it to the Xinzha Patrol Station. Detective Ye Yushan was ordered to investigate. The door was forced open, and Tang's body was taken down. A suicide note was found near his body, which briefly described the reasons for his suicide. The detective then transported the body to the Feilun Road Mortuary. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Diao Chengtang from the First Special District District Court arrived at the mortuary to conduct an autopsy. Chen Meiyu testified that she had known the deceased for three years and had been in a relationship for a year. A week ago, a companion sister's family had an affair to return home, so he ordered me to accompany him for a night. The next day when he returned home, the deceased beat and scolded me because of this, so I went to my sister's place in extreme anger. I am now willing to claim the body. Hua Li, the second landlord, testified that she was thirty years old, from Suzhou, and was the second landlord of the house. They moved in last December. She usually saw the deceased doing laundry and cooking. In the past four or five days, she had not seen either of them. So, at around 10 a.m., she went to take a peek and saw that the door was still tightly closed. She was horrified to see Tang hanging through the crack in the door and reported it to the patrol station. She had not heard anything about their quarrels. Detective Ye Yushan reported the previous circumstances. Mr. Diao then ruled that Tang Guanlin had died by suicide by hanging and ordered that the body be handed over to Chen Meiyu, who had made arrangements for the coffin and burial.

Ferry Workers at Dongjiadu Petition Yesterday 167

Objecting to the Xingtuo Society Taking Over the Ferry Service

According to the Dagong News Agency, since the Dongjiadu Ferry in the South was transferred to the Xingye Trust Society, the ferry workers there feared losing their livelihoods and rose up in protest. They demanded that the workers be allowed to provide their own ferries. Yesterday, the workers sent representatives in groups to petition various Party and government agencies. The first group, led by Zhao Shunxiang, Zhang Xingliang, Ji Gedu, Chen Jinbiao, and more than thirty other representatives, went to the Municipal Government, Public Utilities Bureau, Social Affairs Bureau, Municipal Party Headquarters, and General Labor Union. At the Municipal Government, Section Member Zhu received them and acknowledged that the workers' situation was reasonable. However, the Municipal Government had already approved the transfer to the Xingye Trust Society, so the authority already belonged to the society. The workers then detailed their previous requests for improvements, which had not been approved. Section Member Zhu agreed to forward the matter to the Mayor for review. At the Social Affairs Bureau, Wang Gang met with them on behalf of the director, stating that the case was very important as it concerned unemployment and agreed to forward it to the director for discussion at a bureau meeting. The second group, led by Zhang Zhenliang, went to the Municipal Party Headquarters and Public Utilities Bureau. At the Municipal Party Headquarters, Li Weixiong from the Civil Training Section received them and agreed to convey their message. At the Public Utilities Bureau, Shipping Director Song and Mr. Chen Pengzhan received them, acknowledging the need to protect the workers' livelihoods. Regarding the society's encroachment on the original ferry workers' wharves, they accepted the suggestion and agreed to report to the director for instructions. The petitioning group then went to the General Labor Union to request assistance. Standing Committee Member Ye Xianggao received them and expressed his sincere willingness to provide strong assistance. The workers were satisfied and returned to their respective stations.

Record of Relief Efforts by Two Charity Groups After the Zhabei Fire 168

The China Jisheng Society, in response to the fires at Pujilu and Jingjianglu in Zhabei, which destroyed more than one thousand and several hundred thatched-roof houses, sent Mr. Cheng Ruizhi and others to conduct on-site investigations with representatives from the Zhabei Charity Group, including Mr. Li Changlin. According to their report, on the 11th of this month, they investigated Pujilu, with twelve police officers from the local Public Security Bureau police station as guides. They found 243 extremely poor households, consisting of 743 adults and 518 children. There were also about 200 households of disaster victims who fled after the disaster, making it impossible to verify and issue tickets. The Jingjianglu investigation was conducted on the 12th, with the support of Officer Ouyang Liu from the Fourth District Police Station on Zhongxing Road, who instructed Police Chief Chen Junmaoxiu and a police officer as guides. They found 572 extremely poor households, consisting of 1,687 adults and 1,090 children, which was generally consistent with the list of major disaster households compiled by the Fourth District Police Station. They immediately issued soup relief tickets. It was reported that the two charity groups jointly distributed soup at the Jiyang Bridge soup distribution station on Liuying Road, Zhabei, at 7 a.m. yesterday morning, allowing the disaster victims to feed themselves and temporarily address their immediate needs, as they seek to find a place to settle down.

Coal Industry Association Petitions for Strict Handling of Coal Robberies on the Huangpu River 172

The Coal Industry Association submitted a petition to the Municipal Government and Public Security Bureau yesterday stating that robberies of coal by armed bandits have occurred on the Huangpu River. The petition requested a thorough investigation and strict handling of the matter. According to a letter from the Shanghai Coal and Stone Barge Industry Association, members have reported that a company calling itself the Huangpu River Cargo Protection Company has been gathering hooligans, preparing weapons, and extorting exorbitant insurance fees from coal ships. They threaten to rob coal and commit violence if they are not satisfied, causing extreme anxiety. From the 16th Pier to the Longhua Cement Plant, bandits frequently appear and wreak havoc at night. The association, in addition to reporting to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for strict investigation, specifically requests a unified and thorough investigation. According to a letter from member Yitaixing Coal Company, on the afternoon of March 10th at 7 p.m., the No. 5881 barge hired by their company from the Zhu Ceji Barge Company, loaded with 13 tons of coal, was at the Beizhan Wharf in Dongjiadu when more than a dozen robbers suddenly arrived in a sampan, armed with guns, iron bars, and other weapons, and stole about two tons of coal. The bandits told the Zhu Ce's loading staff that for coal transported from Gaochang Temple to the 16th Pier, both east and west of the Huangpu River, an insurance fee of five cents per ton must be paid, otherwise there would be consequences. The robbery on the 10th must have been committed by those gangs. They requested an investigation. According to a letter from member Yuanxing Coal Company, 80 tons of coal delivered to the Yu Qingji Barge Company on the 9th were loaded onto the Shunfu ship of the Dakang Shipping Company at the Yunnong Floating Pontoon in Nanshi. However, three tons of coal were stolen by hooligans in the vicinity. They requested an investigation. The association stated that the above reports concern armed bandits robbing on the Huangpu River, which not only harms merchants and civilians, but also disrupts local security. The case is serious and cannot be tolerated. They humbly request the government to investigate and strictly handle the matter in accordance with the law, in order to eradicate the bandit threat and secure merchants and civilians.

Another petition from the Coal and Stone Barge Industry Association to the Party and government agencies for strict handling was similar in wording (omitted).

China Economic Credit Cooperative Society Affiliated Amateur Aspiration Society Seeking Members 173

The China Economic Credit Cooperative Society, recognizing that Shanghai is a bustling city and that residents who have no place for suitable self-cultivation outside of work are easily led astray, has established an affiliated Amateur Aspiration Society. Chu Minyi has been hired as the honorary chairman, and Pan Gongzhan and Xu Jigong have been hired as honorary vice-chairmen. Zhang Shouyong, the chairman of the cooperative, serves as the chairman of the society, and Lin Kanghou and Bing Hanping serve as vice-chairmen. The society has a library and recreation room. Members can visit the society at any time to read books and newspapers, play chess, listen to the radio, or engage in other legitimate entertainment. There are also clean rooms with low prices for members to rent, as well as bathrooms and dining rooms. Members who are in urgent need can also apply for interest-free mutual aid funds from the society in accordance with the regulations. This not only addresses a few urgent needs, but also enhances credit. If they wish to take supplementary classes, they can study for free and also have arrangements with famous middle schools in Shanghai to reduce tuition fees. It is truly the only organization in Shanghai for encouraging ambition. Members are divided into three categories: supporting members who are enthusiastic about the society's cause and make every effort to assist; permanent members who pay a one-time membership fee of fifty yuan; and ordinary members who pay an annual membership fee of eight yuan (currently only six yuan during the preferential period). The recruitment is ongoing. Those who wish to join can contact the China Economic Credit Cooperative Society Affiliated Amateur Aspiration Society on Hankou Road.

Shanghai Commercial News: Zhang Jiping's Appeal Case Heard Yesterday 175

Arguments Concluded, Sentence Scheduled for the 20th

The Shanghai Commercial News previously published news of the Xu case, and Ji Juemi sued it for defamation. The First Special District Court initially sentenced Zhang Jiping, the editor-in-chief of the newspaper, to four months in prison. Zhang, dissatisfied with the verdict, hired three lawyers, Wang Youling, Jiang Chiping, and Tang Hao, to file an appeal with the same court. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the appeal was heard. Zhang Jiping, accompanied by lawyer Wang Youling, was present on time. Ji Juemi did not attend but was represented by Cao Shulin and Hu Zhenzhi. Presiding Judge Qian Hongye opened the joint panel for the hearing. Appellant Zhang Jiping stated the grounds for the appeal, briefly stating that news reporters are in a third-party position and have no likes or dislikes regarding news reports. The news in this case was published based on incoming submissions, and he, Zhang, had no prior acquaintance or grievances with Ji Juemi, further proving there was no intention to defame. The initial trial's conviction of intentional defamation was inappropriate and should be overturned.

The presiding judge began discussing the facts of the case and initiated arguments. Lawyers Jiang Chiping, Tang Hao, and Wang Youling successively stood and argued that the appellant had an established practice and no malicious intent. Since there was no explicit provision in the Publication Law, and even under criminal law, it was insufficient to constitute a crime. Criminal intent should be considered based on the motive, environment, and consequences. The appellant's motive was open and honest, the environment provided stimulus, and the result did not harm the plaintiff. They requested a verdict of not guilty based on favorable considerations. Subsequently, the plaintiff's representatives, lawyers Cao and Hu, presented their arguments. The court declared the arguments concluded and scheduled the sentencing for 2:00 PM on the 20th of this month.

Compilation of Bank Inspection Reports 180

Central Bank: 190th Issuance Reserve Inspection Report. In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, the committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the banknotes issued by the bank. The 190th inspection was conducted at the bank's Issuance Bureau on March 10, 1934. The inspection results are announced as follows: (A) Total value of banknotes issued: 69,925,615 silver dollars, including 63,520,746 silver dollar notes and 6,404,869 fractional currency notes. Total value of banknote reserves: 69,925,615 silver dollars, including 57,055,615 silver dollars in cash reserves (53,355,511 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuance vault, 1,737,765 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 1,766,339 silver dollars deposited with other banks) and 12,870,000 silver dollars in guaranteed reserves. (B) Total value of Customs Gold Unit exchange notes issued: 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units. Total value of Customs Gold Unit exchange note reserves: 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units, including 7,351.95 taels of gold, equivalent to 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units at a fixed price of 5.779 Customs Gold Units. In accordance with Article 3 of the Central Bank's exchange note regulations, 60% is held in cash reserves and 40% in guaranteed reserves. The current inspection results show that the cash reserves exceed 60% and the guaranteed reserves are less than 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is made on March 13, 1934, by Li Fuxun, chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, and supervisors Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Ji.

The Four Banks Joint Treasury, jointly established by the Yanyeh, JinCheng, Zhongnan, and Continental Banks, specializes in the issuance of Zhongnan Bank notes. According to the treasury's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with full reserves, with cash reserves accounting for at least 60% and guaranteed reserves accounting for at most 40%. A public announcement is made every week, and the announcement is audited by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The 119th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Treasury on March 10, 1934, is recorded as follows: Value of banknotes in circulation: 25,642,137 yuan. Total value of reserves: 25,642,137 yuan, including 20,542,637 yuan in cash reserves and 5,099,500 yuan in guaranteed reserves.

City News

Laozhenghe Dyeing Factory, both main and branch locations are holding sales. Laozhenghe Dyeing Factory on the east side of Zhengjia Wooden Bridge on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, Shanghai, was established during the Tongzhi era. It specializes in dyeing silk from various provinces and is highly regarded by merchant guilds. For over sixty years, Lu, the manager of the factory, has been aware of the current trends and the renewal of all industries. Therefore, he pioneered the invention of machine dyeing, hired technicians, selected first-class dyes and chemical conditioners, and carefully researched to produce excellent products. He is particularly able to understand the psychology of people in society, truly becoming a pioneer in the national dyeing industry. In 1926, during the 60th-anniversary celebration, he issued discount reservation coupons offering 30% off, leading to an unprecedented expansion of retail business. Recently, to better serve customers, the factory has established a branch at 7 Park Road, Avenue Haig, called Laozhenghe West Factory, which officially opened on March 16th. Both the main and branch factories are holding large sales simultaneously, with a standard discount of 30%.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Night School, recognizing the importance of shorthand for business, industry, academics, and journalism, has added a class in Bingxun Chinese shorthand starting this semester. The purpose is to impart this skill to young people in their spare time to facilitate their work and enhance their status. Therefore, the fees are very low. The tuition fee for one semester is only 8 jiao. To facilitate learning, classes are scheduled from 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM every evening so that those busy with work can also attend. It is reported that this semester is scheduled to start on March 17th. At that time, Yan Esheng, the acting principal of the school, and Yang Bingxun, the inventor of Bingxun shorthand, will give speeches. The number of people going to the school to register has been very enthusiastic in recent days. However, as the semester is about to begin and the number of places is limited, anyone wishing to enroll must register as soon as possible. Those who wish to request a copy of the class charter may write or go directly to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Night School at Tianhougong Bridge.

Reading Questions and Answers

Discussion on Reading Methodology (3) 185

On the 12th, a letter from Mr. Wang in this column prompted us to raise a discussion on reading methodology. On the 13th, the editor gave a general introduction, raising three key points. Today, we will discuss the methodology in more detail. -Editor

This is indeed a very difficult question. Moreover, many people oppose the idea of finding a specific method before reading. For example, Mr. Lin Yutang advocates casual reading, without overly strict rules. Of course, Mr. Lin's lofty ideas are aimed at addressing the drawbacks of the American-style teaching methods that are currently popular in China. We also agree to some extent, but Mr. Lin's views are ultimately a "genius" theory of reading, which is not applicable to ordinary people. Other scholars generally have their own methods. For example, Zen Buddhist disciples travel around, visiting many famous mountains and rivers. Although they may not gain anything concrete from their masters, their own experiences are substantial. They integrate and understand on their own. Although this is also a method, it is uneconomical and cannot be expected of ordinary hardworking people. If we speak in terms of the times, it is not very scientific.

So, what are the so-called scientific methodologies that we can adopt?

We will now put forward several key points for discussion.

First, after we have acquired basic knowledge, for example, someone like Mr. Wang, it is still necessary to continue reading, but not aimless reading for the sake of reading. Rather, it is to study with a specific practical problem as the center, and books are just some materials and opinions for reference. The issue involved here is that you should first grasp the center of the research. Taking practical needs as the starting point of the research is not playing with abstract theories, but rather applying the discovered principles to practice while enriching, nurturing, growing, and unfolding these theories in practice. Theory and practice are inseparably combined and unified into a whole.

For example, a person who studies currency or finance issues should first learn the abstract basic theory. However, a more advanced researcher should not only seek satisfaction in many books on currency or finance issues. He must use the current problems, such as the current silver problem, as the main body of the research, and then browse books on this subject. In this way, the research results you obtain will not only be very practical, but also naturally closer to the truth. The interest in research is also much stronger than simply reading abstract books.

Second, to do the above item completely well, we must also pay attention to a "correlation" effect that cannot be ignored in research. That is to say, taking the above example, the study of the silver problem cannot be limited to only the monetary aspect of minted silver coins or the aspect of producing silver ore. We also cannot only pay attention to the fiscal policy of a certain country or a certain international agreement. We also cannot only seek solutions from the past currency system and the history of silver. If we study today's silver problem from the perspective of the world's population, we should first not ignore the current relations of production and the capital system, as well as the current state of the world economy. We should understand the countermeasures to the economic panic and the general living conditions of the masses under this policy in connection with these issues. Then, the books that a researcher has to read are not limited to those on currency. There are books that need to be read carefully, or only browsed, or look at the table of contents, and copy statistics, truly many and many, and they are all so closely related. Without this kind of relationship, you will go to a narrow area that is far away from the truth. Therefore, although this item comes after the previous item, it is still very important.

Third, knowing the correlation in research is not enough. How should you absorb this diverse knowledge? Even if you spend your entire life's efforts, you may not be able to finish reading the books on a certain issue in the modern publishing world. How do you deal with this difficult problem? The main thing is that you should make a correct assessment of these many materials, calmly observe the various viewpoints of different positions, compare each other, and make careful reading of this vast amount of books and newspapers. Browse, copy, clip, underline, and classify, etc. Then, you are not afraid of too much material. As long as you handle it properly, you can approach various subjects with the most economical time. Not only will you not be blinded by books, these materials will also be in your mind and at your fingertips.

Fourth, do not be too ambitious about a kind of research. You must know that the progress of knowledge has a certain course. The most important thing to pay attention to when reading is the process of reading. We can only complete a certain kind of research with a certain level of learning. You must not try to be clever. "English in 100 Days" does not really mean that you can "speak" English. It teaches you to learn a bit of pidgin English. Learning it can only make you a Western servant. Therefore, the increase of knowledge and a certain kind of researcher should have a certain process. For example, before writing a history of currency, researching the original theory, collecting materials, reading books, reading newspapers, listening to the radio, listening to lectures, visiting antique displays, visiting archaeologists, and traveling to various places are all part of the process. Not only unfolding the fragments of time that are carefully written is the completion of this work. This point should be especially noted for people with shallower academic qualifications. You should not act rashly and produce immature things that are harmful to others. At the same time, you should also know a little about the difficulties of learning, and this difficulty is necessary in the process, so you can continue to do it without being discouraged. In the aspect of reading, difficulties are always overcome step by step, as long as you follow a certain path, in an orderly and gradual manner.

Fifth, you should eliminate unnecessary things from your mind. For example, in a tragic marriage, there should be no "dragon and phoenix wedding cakes" appearing on the stage. If you are focused on a certain kind of research, you should discard all unnecessary things except for those related to it. Conan Doyle said that he did not mix anything in his brain except for knowledge related to detectives. The biggest enlightenment I have gained from reading the Sherlock Holmes detective case is this sentence in the preface of a certain volume. This is the key to the success of his novels, and it is also the key to the success of all learning.

Below, we will discuss in detail various technical aspects of the reading process one by one. (To be continued)

Education News

Other Locations 203

Implementing Rural Improvement: Fujian Union College Establishes Rural Service Department

Researching Rural Revival Plans and Cultivating Rural Work Talents

(Fuzhou Correspondence) The private Fujian Union College is one of the highest institutions of learning in Fujian Province. It has been established for nearly twenty years and has a good reputation. The school is located in the scenic and well-known Shigu Mountain in Min, surrounded by villages. Therefore, it has always paid close attention to rural service and rural issues. In the past six or seven years, the college has used its internal scientific equipment to actively engage in agricultural experiment work, such as grain selection, silkworm improvement, crop pest research, fruit tree cultivation, beekeeping, chicken farming, and frog farming, all of which have achieved considerable results. These results have been introduced to the villagers and have been well-received and beneficial.

Recently Established a Special Department 204

Recently, the college, alarmed by the increasing frequency of rural bankruptcy and the deepening economic panic in the country, established a Rural Service Department to make a practical contribution. Special funds have been allocated to actively implement rural services, plan expenses, and concentrate talent to prepare for improving rural undertakings.

Initial Plans Formulated 205

The initial plans of the Rural Service Department have recently been roughly formulated and divided into two major categories. The first is "Analysis of Rural Needs in this Province": A. Research on rural production issues; B. Research on rural economic issues; C. Research on social life improvement issues. The second is "Measures to Meet Rural Needs": A. Conducting specialized research and special service work; B. Implementing experiments and building a central rural service extension area; C. Training rural service personnel; D. Extension work.

Guidance of Internal Courses 206

To guide the work of the Rural Service Department, the college has established two courses in the Economics and Education Departments: "Rural Cooperation" and "Rural Service Methods." The former focuses on the practical methods of rural cooperation and differs from general lectures that only focus on theory and ignore practical application. The latter trains a group of students to study in classrooms at the college and to go to nearby villages to lead the children in the villages to experience a group life, so that theory and experience can advance hand in hand, and the effectiveness of the work will definitely be doubled.

Experts Responsible for Guidance 207

Since the establishment of the Rural Service Department, the college has hired Chen Xicheng, an alumnus of the college, to return to the college to preside over the work. Mr. Chen has a Ph.D. in economics from Yale University in the United States and has specialized in rural economics for many years. After graduation, he traveled around the world to investigate the state of rural economies. He once went to Denmark to study rural cooperation and has special insights. Mr. Chen has now arrived at the college to take up his post.

Soliciting Cooperative Organizations 208

The college believes that rural revitalization is a major issue related to national economy and people's livelihood, and the procedures are complicated. It cannot be shouldered by one school alone. Recently, President Lin Jingrun has separately invited agricultural experts at home and abroad and enthusiastic social service personnel to cooperate, so that this experiment can proceed smoothly. If it is successful in the future, it may be a great event for national rejuvenation.

News on the Termination and Reorganization of the Film Censorship Committee 209

The issue of film censorship in China was initially proposed by the Ministry of Interior, which wanted to refer to the Japanese method of film censorship, which was carried out by the Tokyo Police Department, so that the Ministry of Interior would carry out the censorship, because the Ministry of Interior has a Police Department, which can preside over everything. Later, the Ministry of Education also proposed that film censorship is related to social education. As a result, the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education jointly organized the Film Censorship Committee, and the two ministries jointly sent seven members to serve concurrently in censorship matters. The Central Party Headquarters also sent three instructors to work on film censorship. The Censorship Committee was attached to the Ministry of Education, and the members continued to receive their original positions and salaries from their respective ministries. The Censorship Committee subsidized each member with 30 yuan for travel expenses. In addition to their duties in the ministry, the members would reduce their duties in the ministry during film censorship. After the proposal to change the members of the committee to full-time and to change the organization, the committee is now affiliated with the Film Industry Guidance Committee of the Central Propaganda Committee (the Guidance Committee is divided into two committees: one is the Film Script Review Committee, and the other is the Film Censorship Committee). After the reorganization, the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education no longer officially send members to participate. The Film Industry Guidance Committee has now hired Luo Gang, Dai Ce, and others as members of the Censorship Committee, with Luo as the director. All the film censorship committees jointly organized by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education will be terminated upon receipt of the order from the Executive Yuan. However, the financial accounts for the past year have not yet been prepared and reported to the Audit Department (in addition to the members, the committee has more than ten administrative staff and is also an affiliated institution). It has been approved to allow two months to complete the accounting. However, film censorship will be handled by the reorganized Censorship Committee around the middle of this month. The film censorship venue on the upper floor of the auditorium of the Ministry of Education is said to be temporarily lent to the reorganized Censorship Committee for three weeks.

Anhui Provincial Two Educational Expenditure Agency Personnel 211

The Anhui Provincial Government recently approved the regulations for the Academic Property Reorganization Committee and the Education Expenditure Committee and plans to establish the two agencies immediately. It is reported that the provincial government has appointed Wu Tianheng as the secretary of the Academic Property Reorganization Committee and Jin Jiechen as the secretary of the Education Expenditure Committee and issued the seals of the two agencies. Secondary Education in Zhejiang Province 212

Qian Jiazhi, secretary of the Zhejiang Provincial Education Department, reported to the provincial government on the secondary education in the province in the past six months, stating that Director Chen reported on the situation of county and city education in the province in the past six months, focusing on qualitative improvement and quantitative advancement. The report on secondary education in the province in the past six months also follows this and describes the plans and improvement methods in two parts.

(1) Plan to Promote Teacher Education and Vocational Education

Affected by the shortage of education funds in the province in recent years, the number of secondary schools has not been expanded as much as possible, and the regulations of the Ministry of Education to reduce ordinary middle schools and establish vocational schools and normal schools have been followed. Therefore, in the future, the department will handle secondary education and adhere to this policy to suit the province's advancement plan. A. Plan to Promote Normal Education: Normal education in the province has been operating for nearly thirty years, and it was once very prosperous, with many talents emerging. Later, due to frequent changes in the education system and laws, mergers and reorganizations gradually reduced the number of normal schools. In the 20th year of the Republic, there were only 1,823 normal school students. After reorganization in the 21st year, the number increased to 2,420. In the 22nd year, the department, according to the current distribution and needs of teacher training institutions, made a multi-year advancement plan, dividing the 76 counties and cities in the province into four regions according to the old routes. Although there is no independently established normal school in the Jinhua region, the provincial Jinhua Middle School still has a senior high school normal department, which has always recruited one class. This year, it was ordered to recruit one more class. As for the Qiantang and Kuaiji regions, there are independent normal schools, but the provincial teacher training institution in the Ouhai region is still vacant. Therefore, a provincial Wenzhou Normal School was added in Zhenglou, Pingyang County. The county or joint normal training institutions were also increased or reorganized as needed. A total of ten have been approved successively. B. Plan to Promote Vocational Education: The department believes that the effectiveness of vocational education has been rare in recent years, and the most important reason is that vocational education cannot adapt to social needs. Therefore, students have no way out, and vocational education gradually becomes rigid. Now, in order to actively promote vocational education, we will examine the needs of the province in detail, establish goals, and use them as the basis for the annual advancement of vocational education. The vocational schools needed in the province must be increased as much as possible. However, vocational schools focus on equipment and practice places. The province's education funds are insufficient, and it is impossible to enrich the quantity and quality at the same time. Now, in this year, based on the principle that agricultural education is the most important in the province, we will first establish an experimental agricultural school in Tangya, Jinhua County, to cultivate agricultural talents who use both hands and brains and actually operate with an experimental spirit. In addition, in recent years, the province has actively reorganized the field tax and miscellaneous taxes and improved the accounting system, and there are also a large number of financial assistants needed. Therefore, a financial specialization class was attached to the commercial department of the provincial Hangzhou Senior High School to meet the needs of the society. In addition, in recent years, the province has been clearing land, building highways, and gradually organizing them, and there is a great need for replacement personnel with simple academic skills in civil engineering. Therefore, a senior civil engineering vocational class was attached to the provincial Jiaxing Junior High School. As for how to follow the regulations of the Ministry of Education in the future, the percentage standard for the establishment of secondary schools has been approved by Director Chen according to the situation in the province. We will train and reorganize secondary education, maintain the status quo, actively expand teacher training and vocational education, raise funds, increase the number of schools, and set a four-year advancement plan to achieve the goal of completing the standard by the 26th year of the Republic.

(2) Measures to Improve Secondary Education

Secondary education is an important process in students' education. We will describe the assessment of teachers and students in two parts. A. Regarding faculty and staff, in the 22nd year of the Republic, the province revised the Interim Regulations on the Administrative Organization of Secondary Schools in the Province and the Interim Regulations on the Appointment, Dismissal, and Treatment of Principals and Teachers of Secondary Schools in the Province in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Education on secondary schools, normal schools, and vocational schools. On the one hand, we will slightly limit the number of secondary school staff to regulate expenses, and on the other hand, we will improve the qualifications of secondary school teachers to increase teaching efficiency. At present, in addition to promulgating the Interim Measures for Reviewing the Qualifications of Secondary School Teachers, we are drafting measures for secondary school teachers to pursue further studies so that teachers in each school can improve their academic discussions and keep up with the times. B. Regarding students, the most important thing implemented in the past six months is (1) fulfilling the secondary school graduation examination, (2) promulgating the plan to guide the thinking of students in secondary schools, and (3) producing and distributing the skill test form for students in secondary schools above the secondary level in Zhejiang Province. If the above assessment of teachers and students can be maintained, the improvement of secondary education in the province will be effective.

Director Pan of the Training Supervisory Department Departs to Inspect Military Training 214

The Municipal Education Bureau Ordered to Notify All Middle Schools

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to all public and registered private high schools in the city yesterday, stating, "According to the order No. 2296 of the Ministry of Education, it is approved by the Training Supervisory Department to investigate the progress of national military education. According to local regulations, the ministry should send personnel from time to time to review the implementation and provide necessary instructions. Personnel have been sent to Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces for on-site inspections, but due to factual obstacles in other provinces and cities, they have not been held. Now that the situation in various places is tending to stabilize and traffic is unobstructed, on-site inspection of national military training in various provinces and cities should be carried out in accordance with regulations to observe results and promote improvement. The ministry has appointed Pan Youqiang, director of the National Military Education Department of the ministry, to depart for Hubei, Henan, Hebei, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Jiangsu to inspect military education in high schools and above and to investigate the situation of local armies and the organization of the masses. In addition to ordering the departure in March and sending separate letters, it is necessary to check and notify them. It is ordered to transfer and notify all public and private high schools and above under your jurisdiction. This order, etc. According to this, we urgently order your school to be notified. This order."
