Essays

The Jaws of the Tiger 225

— Wofo

"The road is like the tiger's mouth; you must not walk in the middle." Indeed, one cannot help but be grateful for the kindness of the admonishers. Automobiles, moreover, countless automobiles, simultaneously flash their two great eyes, filled with a terrifying light, picking out people to devour, weaving together like chasing the wind and electricity. At this moment, you, standing in the jaws of the tiger, if you feel a sudden darkness before your eyes due to carelessness or haste, your heart in a panic, then, in just an instant, the scarlet blood that was originally obediently circulating in the blood vessels around your body, without even being chewed by the tiger's mouth, will stain the wheels, stain the road, and be seen by those in the cars, the drivers, and passersby as peach blossoms in March.

"The road is like the tiger's mouth" is not lying at all. Perhaps its—the automobile's—appetite for eating people is even fiercer than that of a real tiger. Therefore, "you must not walk in the middle," how firmly should you remember this! Remember it until you leave the "tiger's mouth."

But, taking Shanghai as an example... are "roads" the only "tiger's mouths" that are open and waiting to eat people? Having avoided the tiger's mouth of the road, is there no possibility of falling into other "tiger's mouths" again? Frankly speaking... in Shanghai, in addition to "roads," the "tiger's mouths" are simply countless.

All places of intoxication, all places of comfort, all flirtatious glances, fleshy legs, everything... everywhere there is such a "tiger's mouth" open and waiting to eat people. However, the tiger's mouth of the road is tangible, while all these "tiger's mouths" are comparatively intangible. Yet, precisely because they are intangible, you are less likely to feel the terror of the tiger's mouth of the road, be wary, and avoid them in advance. Perhaps not only will you not feel terror, be wary, and avoid them in advance, but you will also think it is very necessary to send your body, life, plus your parents, wife, family property, and career, all together, voluntarily, and sincerely into all these "tiger's mouths." Also, precisely because they are intangible, when you fall into the tiger's mouth of the road, you can still see your scarlet blood staining the wheels, staining the road... but when you fall into all these "tiger's mouths," not even a drop or strand of blood will fly out of that "tiger's mouth," because your entire body has been annihilated. Shanghai "tiger's mouths," are they only "roads"? Having avoided the tiger's mouth of the road, is there no possibility of falling into other "tiger's mouths" again? Yet, people only see the "tiger's mouth" of the road, but never see the other "tiger's mouths." Admonishers also only warn of the "tiger's mouth" of the road, but do not warn of the other "tiger's mouths."

Therefore, people's destination ultimately cannot escape the "tiger's mouth."

Research on Inkstones (II) 226

— Wuliao Ke

(1) The reason for loving inkstones lies in their practicality.

The origin of inkstones is very ancient. It is well known that the Yellow Emperor used jade as an inkstone, and Emperor Hongshi created the ink sea. The Miscellaneous Records of the Western Capital also says that the emperor used jade as an inkstone and wine as a drop, taking it to be non-freezing. Therefore, in later generations, there was still the circulation of yellow jade inkstones and black jade inkstones. In addition to the emperor using jade, other officials and civilians seemed to be able to choose inkstone materials at will, so there were also various types of crystal inkstones, iron inkstones, copper inkstones, magnetic inkstones, and bamboo inkstones. After the Qin and Han dynasties, those who used inkstones began to study inkstone materials and recognized various mountain stones as suitable for practical use. At that time, after many people's tests, the most suitable mountain stones that were confirmed included the Yanzhi stone from Beijing's Meishan Mountain, the Huizhou She stone from Jiangnan, the Lingyan Wu Village stone from Suzhou, the Kaihua black stone from Quzhou, Zhejiang, the Datuo stone from Guizhou in Huguang, the Yuanzhou black stone, the Zhizhou Changde Jianxi stone, the Zijin stone from Shandong, the Hongsi stone from Qingzhou, the Ji Island stone from Dengzhou, the Jiao stone from Jiangzhou, Shanxi, the Lintao Fuhe green stone from Shaanxi, the Zhaoqing Duanxi stone from Guangdong, the Jinxing stone from Qiongzhou, and the Chen Ni inkstone from Guo Prefecture and the Guwa inkstone from Xiang Prefecture (the above stones' properties are all explained in Shi Lianshui and Tang Bingjun's Records of the Four Treasures of the Study). In addition, there are many who use other stones as inkstones, but none are as famous as the above. During the Tang and Song dynasties, the country was peaceful and well-governed, and culture became more advanced. The study of inkstone stones became more meticulous. Among the above inkstone materials, the Duan stone from Zhaoqing, the She stone from Huizhou, and the Chen Ni stone from Guo Prefecture were recognized as particularly suitable. From then on, the three types of Duan, She, and Chen became popular in the world. At that time, the Tao River Tao green inkstone and the Hongsi inkstone from Qingzhou were both regarded as rare and famous stones in the world. However, because they were produced in small quantities and difficult to mine, they were rarely circulated. The Japanese still love them and strive to collect them, but it is said that they are absolutely impossible to obtain.

Among these three types of Duan, She, and Chen, by the Ming and Qing dynasties, Duan gradually became the only one that was valued, because Duan stone was more suitable for practical use than She and Chen. Why is Duan stone suitable for practical use? It is fine, delicate, firm, and moist, does not harm the brush, does not dry easily, and the ink ground on it is finer than on other inkstones, grinding ink quickly and developing ink well. As for the difference between grinding ink quickly and developing ink well, Ji Shouqiao of Xiushui said in his Study of Duanxi Inkstones that Duke Mi Zhao and others all said that the wonder of developing ink is like lacquer and oil. It is also said that the stone from the lower rock develops ink as smoothly as boiling pan and sticking wax. Su Dongpo said, "The beauty of an inkstone lies only in its smoothness and ability to develop ink." Cai Junmo's discussion is especially clear and distinct, directly saying that developing ink is not easy to grind. The ink in the inkstone shines brightly, rotating with the brush, and when washed, it dissolves completely. It is because the stone is firm and moist and can develop it without sticking to the inkstone. Therefore, those who know consider easy grinding to be grinding ink quickly, and ink like oil to be developing ink. The best of the water pit can combine both, but it is wrong to consider easy grinding to be developing ink.

What is called suitable for practical use, its wonderfulness lies entirely in this. Today's inkstone lovers all love water rocks, precisely for this reason. From this, we can also prove my statement that the reason for loving inkstones lies in practicality. Errata: In yesterday's article on Research on Inkstones, in the sentence "天上神仙一句," the word "上" was misprinted as "下." This is specifically corrected.

In a Dream 227

— Shijiu

The sky that day did not seem to have sunlight. On an unknown street, there were many Boy Scouts strolling idly in twos and threes. Not far from this street, there seemed to be a broad square, like a public sports field. The walls were white, and groups of Boy Scouts were walking in and out of an arched door. This square was their gathering place.

I don't know how, but I was also walking on this street, as if I was escorting my family back to my hometown, passing by this place. As I was walking, I suddenly met her face to face. I still remember very clearly that although her face was fairer than before, she had lost some weight. She didn't seem to see me. I, for some reason, wanted to call out to her, but in the end, I didn't. After we brushed past each other, I turned my head to look at her, and she stopped and called out to me, "Sir." Then, she said, "Please come with me."

We walked to the front of a house. The doorway was very narrow, and she went in. I don't know why, but I didn't follow her in; I just stood outside the door. Ah! The bugle suddenly sounded loudly, and she hurriedly came out. I said, "This is the order to assemble; you should go quickly."

I watched her go, feeling deeply disappointed. I still remember very clearly that the clothes she was wearing were still that light-colored liberty cloth shirt.

Blush 228

— Mingyi

The Red Route 7 bus coming out of Xujiahui was packed with students from × school. Apart from the glittering heads and feet, there were also very smart Western suits. Coincidentally, the seats in the bus were just full. The bus started, and they also began to talk about ways to spend this Sunday. "Let's go to the Cathay to see Barrymore!" "No, let's get a haircut first." "I heard that business at the Balunmen Dance Hall is not bad. If we go later, there might be surprises." Due to the disagreement of opinions, no good result was achieved in the short time.

The fast bus kept shortening its route. One stop after another was passed. At the intersection of Haig Road and Yidingpan Road, the bus stopped. A fashionable young lady got on. She had a healthy and beautiful physique, full of the majesty of a virgin, lively, with dimpled smiles. She was truly worthy of being the school belle of × school.

The bus continued to speed forward as if flying. One stop after another was passed, the red Jing'an Temple, the yellow post office. At the last stop, the true face of the metropolis was seen again, beautiful concubines, drawing eyebrows, applying powder, fully expressing vanity and extravagance. Enjoy today while you have wine, for tomorrow you may be drunk. Alas! In the great universe, there is originally only one "happiness" that is worth cherishing. The bus stopped. One by one, people emerged from the carriage with smiles, and of course, not a little bit of shy blush appeared on her lively and charming face.

Correction: In the article "Wang Jingwei's Obsession with Eating Chicks" published in this journal the day before yesterday, it was said that Jiang ate three chicks in one meal and killed three to four thousand chicks a year, etc. The author's words were too extreme and did not reflect the facts. It should be corrected immediately.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 229

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Five

Tearful Faces See People Off to Distant Garrisons, Wind and Sand Pervade the Night, Leaving the Fortress, Stationing in a Lonely City

Secondly, it just so happens that the northeast wind is blowing tonight. People just have to walk against the wind, and that will be heading northeast, there will be no mistake. However, the road underfoot is not necessarily heading directly northeast, so after walking a short distance, one has to stop and consider for a moment. Moreover, a battalion of people forming four lines, when stretched out, is quite long, and it is not easy to see each other from front to back. Although each company has white flags held up as contact markers, the night is too dark, and it is not clear. In addition, the wind outside the pass, squeezed out of the mountain valleys, is particularly strong, blowing people's hair back and making it impossible to lift their heads. After walking for two or three hours, they had not even covered twenty miles, and everyone was exhausted. They had no choice but to grope for a while and rest for a while. Later, they managed to grope their way to a large grove of trees, which offered some shelter from the wind. They announced a rest at the foot of the grove on the hillside. All that could be heard was the wind blowing through the treetops, the wind rushing in with a "whoosh," the branches sweeping back with a "swish." Although it was not as fierce as the artillery fire on the battlefield, it was even more tragic and fierce than the artillery fire on the battlefield. Everyone sat with their guns propped up on the dark hillside. It was the waning moon, about three hours after midnight. The night gradually brightened. Although the wind and sand in the air were still heavy, the scenery in front of them could slowly be seen clearly. At the same time, they discovered a road running through the middle of two mountain peaks, curving past. If this were military marching in wartime, this would be the easiest place to be ambushed, and it was impossible to stay. The four company commanders could not help but sweat in their hearts. Shi Fang stood up, looked around, checked his luminous wristwatch, and ordered them to continue marching. The soldiers struggled forward against the wind and sand, not knowing what the mission was. Everyone guessed that it was fighting, but they also did not see it as a peaceful task. They had no choice but to keep a riddle in their hearts and walk along in a daze. (335)

Short Story

Buying an Umbrella 230

— Jian

At the western end of the new market, a moat-like small river cleverly displays a bit of its role as a boundary. The river is very narrow, but a rather wide plank bridge is built over it. From here, you can go to the West City, or you can take a turn and take a shortcut to the South City. This is the road I have to travel back and forth twice a day. The reason is that I am a regular visitor to the new market. If you can't find me in those singing halls every night, that would truly be a miracle.

Initially, near this riverbank, there were only one or two bird shops and a small wine shop. In front of the wooden bridge, there was a bit of a commercial appearance. At night, the light of just one electric lamp often made me worry about whether I would fall into the river when taking a rickshaw across the bridge. But soon the place gradually prospered. The number of shops increased from three or two to a dozen. There were tea houses, noodle shops, fortune-telling shops, and even a foreign goods shop with a broadcasting machine. Every day, some scratchy music sounds spread from there, attracting many unhealthy women, filthy children, and anemic, rough laborers.

After a certain appropriate time in the evening, many shops that did not need to do evening business closed their doors and took a break. Only one noodle shop remained open because it had to provide dinner for the rickshaw pullers. The electric light leaking from there was as weak as the light of a candle. Gradually, I saw several women standing side by side in front of the noodle shop. A few pieces of cheap, colorful clothing haphazardly reflected a certain type of human figure that we often see on Fuzhou Road in Shanghai. I didn't observe them closely, but in a hasty glance, some feelings couldn't help but float to my heart... "Ah, there are street prostitutes here too. The influence of Shanghai-style street prostitutes has openly invaded this small city."

The rickshaw pullers were accustomed to using these street prostitutes as objects of ridicule. When they dragged guests up the bridge, they often intentionally rudely rubbed past them, or simply charged straight at them. The street prostitutes were forced to retreat and curse. One day, late at night, I finished listening to the opera in the market and took a rickshaw back. Unexpectedly, I encountered a heavy rain. The rickshaw puller's oilskin coat and the oilcloth on the rickshaw both excitedly bounced with raindrops. When passing over this wooden bridge, the street prostitute that I usually saw was the only one lingering there. The large red flower clothes could be seen in the darkness, all stuck together in a mess. The powder on her face was washed away, showing streaks. Many water droplets glistened on her hair. This was a very ugly street prostitute, often the unluckiest loner in that usual line. She slowly walked towards us. When my rickshaw brushed past her, she suddenly stopped and hurriedly cast a heavy arrow of sight over, which was a pair of eyes that did not shine at all, containing much complex sorrow. I did not dare to look her directly in the eyes, and only captured the roughest impression before hurriedly passing by.

The rain continued intermittently for two days and two nights. When returning home from the new market at night, under the oilcloth of the rickshaw, I imagined the miserable street prostitute standing in the rain waiting for business, but I no longer saw her. The light leaking from the noodle shop was still so dim and worried, but in front of the door, there was no one there.

Unexpectedly, on the third day, I saw that street prostitute buying an umbrella in a foreign goods shop on another street. It was daytime, and the weather was clear. The price she paid for the umbrella was eleven coppers for six jiao small foreign coins. She held the umbrella in a very wealthy and leisurely manner and walked out of the shop door, parallel to me. She seemed to have awakened some memory and looked at me deeply, still with a pair of eyes that did not shine at all, but the sorrow was even more complex.

Afterwards, I no longer saw that street prostitute on the market by the river, whether it was sunny or raining. But often I could still see some other street prostitutes walking back and forth under umbrellas in the rain, and I thought of her. She, this street wanderer who experiences all kinds of pain in the human world, had a different fate. She has already gone to another world, perhaps.

Commercial News

Financial Gold Price Slightly Declines by One and a Half Yuan 231

American Proposal to Issue Paper Money and Purchase Silver Meets Weak Performance

Central Bank Opens Spot Market for Over Eight Hundred Bars, Briefly Rising

The gold market slightly rebounded yesterday. Unfavorable foreign news and the Central Bank's opening of the spot market balanced the day's situation. In the morning, overseas silver markets in England and America rose in unison, with silver prices on the London Metal Exchange rising between 3.7 and 5.8 basis points. London's raw gold fell by half a penny, and exchange rates also rose, with American wheat rising by 1.125 points and American cotton rising by 12 pounds. The opening for wool was flat, and although it once rose to three yuan afterward, due to news from the Associated Press that the American government planned to issue paper money to aid wounded soldiers, it weakened slightly. After the opening, prices fluctuated. A Reuters dispatch reported that U.S. Senator Wheeler had proposed a mutual reconciliation plan, leading to a proposal within the U.S. government to purchase 50,000,000 ounces of silver monthly, aiming for a gold-silver ratio of 16 to 1. This news still struggled to maintain prices. Later, banks continued to buy forward U.S. exchange, and the Central Bank opened the spot market for over eight hundred bars (at a price of 4.5 yuan), causing prices to rise temporarily, but they slightly receded at noon. The market sentiment was weaker in the afternoon, and the exchange market seemed looser. Although Bombay saw a decline, rumors of British purchases of silver through private Western telegrams circulated. Market sentiment was sluggish, and prices slightly declined. Refined gold was priced at 55 yuan. The four-five month swap will begin at 3:00 PM on the 15th, marking the first swap after the new standard. There was much speculation on both sides, but the premium was not expected to be too large. The day's market conditions are recorded as follows:

The morning opening was 942.6 yuan, slightly higher by 1.6 yuan compared to the previous close. Goods opened at 2.4 yuan. The exchange market opened with recent selling prices of British exchange at 1 shilling, 4 pence, 5625, and U.S. exchange at 35.25 yuan. While Zhifeng Yong reached 3.2 yuan, a Reuters dispatch of silver purchases caused Shengda Lai to sell, and Pan Gen and Mitsui to offer six-month U.S. dollars at 6875, causing the price to fall to within 2 yuan. Qian Changxiang and Huixiang Lai bought in, causing it to rise again to above 3 yuan. Shengda and Dadecheng continued to sell, causing it to fall to 1.8 yuan. Anticipating that HSBC would quote British exchange at flat and U.S. exchange up 125, market sentiment stabilized. New York Stock Market Rises 236

Xinfeng Foreign Firm reported on the 12th that the New York stock market was firm throughout the day. Later, due to a sharp rise in the value of goods, and with bonds strong, the market situation continued to rise. The strength of goods and bonds was due to the resurgence of inflation concerns, which may be related to the veteran's pension proposal. US public debt and other high-grade bonds fell slightly, and foreign debt was mixed. The total daily trading volume was 1.26 million shares. The supply of wheat decreased from 3,518,000 to 97,122,000 bushels, the smallest number since 1929. Last year's total was 142,431,000 bushels. Prices increased due to the shortage. The cotton market was not very concerned about the impending passage of the Bankhead Act. If it passes and prices rise, bullish traders may take profits at the high, and the market may have a reaction. However, the spot market position is strong and commerce will continue to develop, so it is possible to buy low at that time. The firm also received a report from the New York Standard Statistics Company stating that commercial progress and confidence in corporate profitability are sufficient to overcome the unease caused by overly intrusive legislation and labor proposals. The market situation will go through another period of hesitation, but the long-term trend is bound to be upward. However, investment strategies must be prudent. Stocks that can directly benefit from the recovery should be retained, but it is temporarily not advisable to make further purchases, so as to reserve sufficient purchasing power to await the arrival of opportunities. The recovery of various companies is uneven, but the position of bonds should not be adversely affected, so medium and secondary excellent bonds can be retained or repurchased. The general importance of increasing wages and reducing working hours is overstated, as the party authorities have no intention of forcing all factories to implement them uniformly. Industrial production in March is expected to be 2% higher than in February. Although the proposal to restrict speculation will be amended, it is still difficult to predict exactly how it will be. Free Talk

Protest by the German Ambassador to the U.S. 271

— Yu Dafu

According to an eight-day Reuters dispatch: "A large-scale mock trial was held in a certain park in New York last night, with German Chancellor Hitler as the defendant. As a result, Hitler was found guilty of destroying civilization. The German Ambassador to the U.S. lodged a protest with the White House, but it was rejected," and so on.

Seeing the words "mock trial" reminded me of many similar things. There is a Dongyue Temple, commonly known as the Old Dongyue Temple, at the foot of Fahua Mountain in Beilang, Hangzhou. The spring and autumn temple fairs are more lively than any large-scale exhibition. Trials are also held, with the Great Emperor of Dongyue presiding over the court. The bailiffs, clerks, soldiers, yakshas, and impermanent ghosts are all played by living people who have offered sacrifices at the grave. Cauldrons, saws, yokes, iron chains, and all the cruel instruments of torture that exist in the world are prepared. It is said that those suffering from incurable diseases, such as madness that cannot be cured by medicine, only need to go up the mountain in the middle of the night and undergo a court trial once, and the illness will be cured. Therefore, ignorant villagers go to participate in this kind of court trial every year, with the number of people reaching about 30,000 to 50,000 per quarter. This can be regarded as one of the grandest mock trials.

Secondly, I have also seen a Kunqu opera called "Beating the Drum and Scolding Cao." It is said that it was originally a kind of the "Four Cries of the Gibbon" script written by Xu Wenchang. The scene in the play is that in the Yama Hall, Miheng, wearing light fur and loose robes, calls Yama his brother. Suddenly, a ghost soldier leads a prisoner with a disheveled beard and a face covered in shackles. After Yama and Miheng discuss it, they order the ghost soldiers to open the shackles, take off the prisoner's clothes, and put on red robes and jade belts, dressing him up as Cao Cao on the stage. Miheng also takes off his light fur, puts on tattered clothes, and re-enacts a good play of "Beating the Drum and Scolding Cao." After the play is over, Cao Cao, dressed as a Prime Minister, is teased and beaten by the ghost soldiers a few times, then put back in his prison clothes, shackled, and dragged back into hell. Scholar Mi and Yama drink a few cups of wine and then disperse. Yama even bows and personally sends him out of the hall. This can be regarded as a mock trial in the pen of a literati, to let Miheng's ghost breathe a sigh of relief. As for the iron statues in front of Yue Fei's tomb and the solemnity of the Yu Zhongsu Temple, that is a case turned over after generations, and should naturally be discussed separately. Thinking back to Hitler, he is the kind of person Confucius spoke of who "only fears that he will die without being known or praised." Therefore, he imitates Mussolini's every move. Therefore, a British correspondent said: "Mussolini is a Statesman, but he is a Stageman." It is similar to saying that Sun Shuao is a noble scholar, and the one who wears the clothes of Youmeng is an actor. But after Bismarck and Wilhelm II, Germany has actually produced another outstanding person of the world, so that he is imitated in mock trials. Hitler himself is certainly satisfied, and the German ambassador is really ignorant and still wants to lodge a protest?

Thoughts Provoked by the Left-Lapel 272

— Liu Ming

On the train from Myitkyina to Mandalay in Upper Burma, the passengers were mostly Burmese and Bai people, needless to say. Just the sight of the men wearing red, green, and colorful skirts like women is enough to evoke a strong exotic mood in the traveler's heart. As for the women, in addition to wearing skirts of various colors, their upper bodies are all in snow-white gauze clothes, and some of the buttons are sewn on the left side. Such peculiar attire immediately reminds one of the people of the ancient State of Chu. According to ancient books, the people of the State of Chu originally wore their lapels on the left. Confucius once sighed like this when praising Guan Zhong's victory over Chu: "Without Guan Zhong, we would be wearing our hair loose and our lapels on the left." Now, in the old land of Chu, Hunan and Hubei, I imagine there are no traces of such attire, but in Upper Burma, I have found it and seen it.

If we take these impressions as a hypothetical proof and add research on race and language, then I dare to say for the time being that the ancient Chu people have not disappeared, but have gradually moved south. However, they are not the current Burmese people (the Burmese, according to "The Tribes of Burma," are a people from the Tibetan Plateau, the same as the Tibetans and the wild people of the Savage Mountain), but the Bai people of Yunnan, the Shan people of Burma (the British call the Bai "Chinese Shan," the Shan "Burmese Shan," and the people of Yunnan call the Shan "Big-Eared Bai"), and the people of Siam. They live in Yunnan in the river basins of the Nu River and the Binlang River (also known as the Daying River, Taiping River, etc.). In Burma, they live in the mountains along the Salween River (the lower reaches of the Nu River in Yunnan) and on both banks of the Irrawaddy River in Upper Burma (the Binlang River in Yunnan flows into the Irrawaddy River at Bhamo). In Siam, almost all the important cities can be said to be theirs. As for language, most of them are the same, but there are also small differences. For example, the very common noun "to eat rice," the Siamese and Shan people call it "King Kao," while the Bai call it "King Hao." And the writing is also the same. According to Xie Bin's "Travels in Yunnan," the Bai use Burmese writing, which is wrong. It can only be said that they use Siamese writing, because the book he based it on is "The Brief History of the Borders of Pusi," compiled by Ke Shuxun, who was responsible for the borders of Pusi in Yunnan, and the area along the borders of Pusi is precisely where the Shan people live, bordering Siam.

The above explains that the Bai, Shan, and Siamese people are one people. As for the proof that they migrated from the Yangtze River in China? This depends on the history of Siam. The origin chapter cites the theory of an Italian linguist, who said that the Siamese people migrated from the Yangtze River basin in China in the 2nd and 3rd centuries AD, because their language still has similarities with the roots of the language of the Chinese people south of the Yangtze River today. As far as I know, several numbers like one, two, three, four, five... in the Zhangquan dialect of Fujian, the Chaozhou dialect of Guangdong, and the Qiongya dialect are exactly the same as what the Bai say. Also, the Bai call "dawn" "Fa Liang," and the meaning of the word "Liang" is the same as our general Mandarin. There is also the dialect of the Chengdu Plain in Sichuan, which calls "distilled grains" "Lao Cao," and the Bai call "eating wine" "King Lao," which is similar again. There are many other similar examples, but due to space limitations, I will not list them all.

Because of the linguistic evidence, and seeing the women's clothes with the left lapel, the hypothesis that the Chu people moved south floated into my mind. Whether this speculation is valid naturally requires detailed research. This article, as the title suggests, is only a beginning.

Folk Songs

Sister Sends Off Brother 273

— Chen Lu

Red cotton pants, green lining, cannot compare to the daughter at her mother's home; at mother's home, she sleeps until breakfast is ready, in her in-law's home, she can't even wait for the rooster to crow.

Rice is cooked in the pot, steamed in the earthenware jar, my brother comes just as we're getting to know each other.

Thinking of keeping my brother for a meal, asking my parents-in-law, they don't say a word.

Sending him off to the front door, I hold my brother's hand.

Sending him off to the bamboo fence, I hold my brother and have a chat.

Sending him off to the water chestnut pond, the water chestnuts bloom, white and vast.

Sending him off to the turtledove's nest, the turtledove smiles at me.

Turtledove, don't laugh at me, I am "Sister Sending Off Brother".

Miscellaneous Notes on Returning South (Continued) 274

— Tang

(Four) Anniversary Memorial "The years are truly aimless, but I still have to endure, since death has not yet come, the joys of life have abandoned me." This is the last stanza of my elegy, written after my father passed away last year, and now it has been a full year. In this year, I don't understand how I have been living, I have just been "enduring." The family has gone through many storms again, and although my mother is managing things, the greatest responsibility still falls on me. Whenever I feel depressed, I often think of writing something about my father, but I never get around to it.

The biggest problem in the family is the economy. In fact, the talk of poverty has been around for a long time, but at that time, relying on my father's reputation, we could still manage to make ends meet. Moreover, my father, like my mother, placed half of his hopes on me, and they tightly concealed the deteriorating state of the family, not letting me know anything. On the surface, guests came and went, and everything inside and out was busy with social interactions, bustling and lively, almost like prosperity. How could I ever have experienced the feeling of being completely impoverished! I only knew that they always had the same smiling face when they saw me. How could I know that behind this smiling face, they were hiding a bitterness more bitter than Coptis chinensis!

I now cherish my childhood because in my childhood there was innocence and happiness. And I know that my innocence and happiness were woven from two sorrowful and compassionate hearts.

But the true meaning of life finally pulled me out of the circle of happiness. After several attacks of worries, my father fell ill in the summer four years ago. First, he had spasms in his limbs and confusion of his mind, and then he turned into mild epilepsy, which came and went from time to time. And then on this day a year ago, on a quiet winter afternoon, he quietly left this world. He wasn't even fifty years old, but he had to go, he wasn't even fifty years old!

Now, now it is a full year.

On this anniversary, because it is New Year's Eve, it is said that even crying must be avoided. I don't even have the freedom to shed a single tear. This time, we won't hold a Taoist ceremony or Buddhist service, just offer a few bowls of fruit, a few plates of dishes, burn a pot of incense, and quietly commemorate this endless sorrow.

We all held back our tears, endured the grief in our hearts, and felt a surge of sourness in our noses.

My mother burned the paper money. I watched the ashes fly up from the ground, and then watched two crystal-clear tears flow from the corner of my mother's eyes. I understood the true meaning of life. Relying on two arms and a brain, I am ready to live on!

○ ○ ○

On "Branding" 275

— Mu Mutian

"Branding" by the young poet Zang Kejia is the most noteworthy collection of poems recently. The author experienced the bankruptcy of the Chinese countryside after the "September 18th Incident" and felt the profound pain of life. He sings about them in poetry with realistic and ordinary materials. He also sings about his own personal experience of the bitterness of life. His short poems can be said to be one side of the symbol of the poetic era.

Although living under the influence of the "Crescent Moon" poets, Zang Kejia, in terms of the form of poetry, has adopted the free verse of the petty bourgeoisie, which is also a noteworthy point of his psychological consciousness. In the heart of this young man, there are quite a few demands for liberalism.

But although he subjectively demands liberalism, the old remnants are constantly binding him. In his body, it seems that there are two forces constantly conflicting with each other and hindering each other, making him unable to develop either aspect as he wishes. I think that in the end, one side will win. This depends on which side he strives to lean towards in the future.

Throughout the small collection of poems "Branding," it reflects the disharmony between Zang's idealism and realism, and the disharmony between the poet's personal expression and his social expression. This disharmony prevents him from completing his liberalism and achieving his goal of self-liberation.

From the collapsing countryside, he saw the cities of the semi-colonies in economic panic. This contradiction arose in his small and weak heart, which is by no means accidental.

He savors his own "philosophy of life" in his heart. Judging from his poems, his inner life is quite profound. His inner life experience made him create his philosophy of life of perseverance and imprison himself. If you want to find his philosophy in his poems, Stoicism is everywhere. From the countryside to the city, he saw all the troubles in the modern city. Cars, trams, the electric lights at night, the intoxication of the flesh, jazz music, etc., all the evils of the city, fraud, deception, and all kinds of strange shady scenes, made him feel that it is difficult to walk in the world. Unable to adapt to this new environment, he felt that...this is not just messing around for fun, this is life, ten thousand hidden arrows are lurking around you, waiting for you to be careless in a thousand precautions.

("Life")

He curses the "ghost-like crowds" in the city at night ("The Night of the City"). He cannot use his reason to analyze society and grasp reality. He cannot scientifically organize his impressions and thus gain correct knowledge. He hopes conceptually, and reaches disillusionment through hope. Therefore, he "remembers only a patch of black shadows" and wants to "recognize life from the needle." He doubts, he feels emptiness. In the end, he creates his philosophy of "living by chewing on bitterness." This Stoicism matches all the poems in "Branding." (To be continued)

Dusk (Four) 276

— Jin Yi

Every morning, waking up from a comfortable sleep, the sunlight shining through the window screen has already covered their beds and the floor. Good dreams may still linger in their minds, but thinking of the long days, they frown slightly again. Although everything is so good materially, there is always something missing. They all know this lack very well, and it has become irreparable. At this time, the maid will quietly push open the door and walk in, and if there is no wind or rain, she will open the windows for them first. Waves of lilac or magnolia fragrance will pour in from the window. They put on their clothes, get out of bed, and stare blankly at the beautiful scenery outside the window.

If it is spring, they can see the ground exuding the breath of spring, and they seem to be able to hear the sound of grass roots sprouting in the soil, and the willow branches swaying softly and long in the wind. The maid will surely say gently: "Miss, don't just stand by the window, the spring breeze is cold. The bath water has been prepared." So they drag their lazier steps reluctantly to the bathroom, and then, after twenty or thirty minutes, they walk out wearily, with their hair scattered over their shoulders. The maid has already closed the window for them at this time, and then brings in breakfast.

After getting dressed, their self-determined work begins. Sometimes they copy calligraphy or draw meticulous figures, sometimes they play the guqin, or Qing Song listens attentively to Qing Zhi blowing the xiao, and the days pass by seemingly easily.

Because they were worried that they were too lonely, the family members used to come to their rooms often, but they immediately saw that they were not interested, and except for their mother, they even showed a little annoyance. So they agreed not to disturb them anymore. When they see people, they hardly say a word, and they show a very unnatural expression, but they don't say anything embarrassing. They just frown or show a helpless look.

Outside this room, this family becomes floating. Qing Shi's wife once cried and made a fuss because Qing Shi did not return all night. Sometimes, she woke up the sleeping people in the middle of the night because the two-year-old child cried for too long, and the mother wondered if there was something wrong with him. Or there was something unclear between the male and female servants... but these things cannot affect them, and even the sounds of the noise are blocked by the doors and windows, becoming extremely faint or non-existent.

Sometimes, Qing Song seems to be completely captured by painting. She draws patiently, and allows two sick-looking red flushes to appear on her pale yellow cheeks because her head has been lowered for too long, and she also reveals a bit of panic as she searches for different colored and ink brushes. Occasionally, a trace of a smile appears on her face, and she still works quietly on her work. Qing Zhi, who is reading a novel, will surely say to him or her.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

The Kalachakra Dharma Assembly 277

— Qiong Sheng

Our China is a country with flourishing culture, so it has always valued courtesy and cherished peace. This spirit has been passed down to the present, and its merits are already beyond instruction. In addition, after Xuanzang's "Journey to the West" brought back the Vajra from the Southern Hua, it was even more evident that everything in the world is nothing but flowers in a mirror and the moon in the water, that is, form is emptiness, and its influence is unknown how many people it has poisoned. However, the general proponents of national essence spare no effort to shout and scream, regarding it as the "ancient civilization" of the Yanhuang Sage, and the foundation of China's national destiny and people's fortune.

This fact is manifested so that we can see it anytime and anywhere... praying for "one side of tranquility" and seeking "avoidance of disasters" is truly a matter of national destiny and the survival of the nation. The reason why my country has become so magnificent is that everyone holds the view that the hardships of life are caused by past lives in samsara. All living beings, the vast world, and many "ill-fated" events in the world are caused by the will of heaven and the divine decree in the underworld.

China is currently in a time of great trouble. Natural disasters, man-made disasters, domestic troubles, and foreign invasions are really coming one after another, making the whole country unable to live or die. In this fiery heat, we are now using our "ancient" magic weapon to find a way out through the hot pursuit of "sincerity brings spirituality." After the September 18th Incident, when the national crisis was imminent, the Panchen Lama was invited to hold the Kalachakra Dharma Assembly in Beiping, and the Great Light Water and Land Dojo was opened. After the Battle of Shanghai, in the ashes, there was also a temporary "National Crisis Dojo" to pray for peace. These are the most obvious examples. As for the many "benevolent people and good men" who take the world as their responsibility, they often advocate writing scriptures, reciting repentance, and building Buddhist halls after their worries, which is almost extremely popular. Examining its meaning and tracing its heart, it is natural to have the desire to eliminate national disasters and save the crisis, but according to the law of the jungle, whether it will make us "have whatever we ask for" is once again vague and speculative.

Do we not see that the smoke of war in Shanghai has just ceased, and bombing sounds have been heard in Luan and Yu. As for the autonomy of Inner Mongolia, the independence of Southern Xinjiang, the invasion of Southwesterners, and the rebellion in Fujian, they all indicate that not only has the crisis not been eliminated and the national disaster not been resolved, but it seems that crises are lurking everywhere, with fire coming out of every hole and smoke rising from every crevice. However, this is because the Chinese nation has deep sins and cannot escape the calamity, and it is not that the prayers are insufficient.

Although it is said that heaven's will is like this, and the descendants of Yan and Huang should be unlucky, but rather than sitting and waiting for death, why not try to do a little "human affairs" in despair? This is why our eminent monks who rely on Buddhism still want to make persistent efforts to seek liberation, and use the supernatural powers of the "Living Buddha" to save China from danger. At that time, the treasure hall will be filled with clouds, and the incense will be curling, and there will be a grand scene.

If burning incense and worshiping Buddha could drive away evil and avoid disasters, then the Boxers of the late Qing Dynasty would have already succeeded, and we would not have to wait for the Kalachakra Dharma Assembly now. Chinese people are superstitious, often thinking of taking the enemy's head from a thousand miles away with leather armor and flying swords. The Panchen Lama's magic is boundless. After this prayer, it can make those invaders repent and change their ways. Then let me kneel down three times and kowtow nine times here, and recite a few "Namo Amitabha".

Autumn of Many Events in the Literary World 278

— A Beggar Writer

I, this beggar, came into the world late. The extravagant lifestyles of my friends, like Dragon Soaring Phoenix Dancing, and the amorous affairs of love story writers who kept mistresses, I was unable to witness, which is a lifelong regret. But crows are black the world over; from one instance, you can infer three. In this corner of a thousand-mile expanse, the land is lively enough.

A random essay about groping buttocks, liberation verses for playing mahjong, sparked a battle like the Chu-Han Contention. This newfangled stuff really caused a sensation, more pleasing to the eye than models swaying their fat hips and twisting their waists. One wave subsides, and another rises. The Beijing-Shanghai literary war was even more thunderous, with direct hand-to-hand combat, making it extremely enjoyable.

Having watched one act after another, it's truly dazzling, and one can't help but shout "Bravo!"

Although the tricks of the old guard are genuine skills, how can the young heroes quietly submit? It's perfectly fine to hold and play with trinkets, but there's no harm in competing. They too stage a continuous, excellent show. "The younger generation is to be feared," this humble beggar can't help but sigh three times, putting down my pen.

Submitting one's own works for others to publish seems to have existed since ancient times. Many so-called writers have built Western-style houses through such means. But having voluntarily agreed (presumably not through coercion) beforehand, why regret it later? It's said that such buried talents can be measured by cartloads. Probably, for the sake of not burying talent, a case of indecency involving someone under sixteen years old was made. As for the content, it will naturally be fairly judged by legal experts; I won't elaborate here.

This case is somewhat more serious than the previous two. This humble beggar is not promoting chaos and stirring up trouble, but even telescopes sometimes get dust particles flying into them. However, while playing mahjong requires the courage to start a major conflict, this double-edged case concerning the guest seat – the literary world – and future reputation, I wonder what the "masters" have to say about it!

Another Love Story 279

— Dai Ni

Hometown Jottings

I said goodbye to my uncle in Shanghai and ran downstairs. In the common room, I met my eldest cousin, who was already a mother of three. She asked me when I would be back and if I had met Sister ×.

A shadow flashed across my mind, seven or eight years ago!

Every New Year, my uncle would keep me at his house, and I often forgot the start of school. A foster daughter of my uncle's also occupied the place.

"They make a great couple!" my uncle would say jokingly after drinking in the evening.

"A little married couple!" the cousins would seize on the remark, gossiping without restraint.

We knew to blush and avoid each other. But – when no one was watching, we would smile at each other.

One morning before the sun rose, a letter was handed to me.

That letter, preserving seven or eight years of time, remained in my bookcase in my hometown, forever after.

"Brother, we can't talk anymore, it's really annoying!

This semester, I'm applying to Shanghai ×× Girls' School. If I'm accepted, we can meet in Shanghai. I'm going home today."

Unable to verify the original, I retained as much of the original essence as possible. We met in Shanghai. My uncle's jest became reality – we were truly in love. The love continued... One year, two years, three years... She graduated from junior high. The student became a teacher. Every week, we were the proud figures of Shanghai. The love continued intermittently.

Another teacher was pursuing her. One day, she handed me a letter – a sweet love letter. "What's the meaning of this?" I casually asked. "It can be read as a collection of love letters." She smiled. "The one in the Western suit?" She nodded. The first kiss of first love. The love continued intermittently. Four years. Five years, six years...

A letter arrived from the post office. "Life is too boring. I took two days off from school. Staying at my eldest sister's house last night (the eldest sister who is a mother of three) was also meaningless. Tonight, shall we go to Donghua (now Paris) to see 'Love Tragedy'? Whoever arrives first waits for the other."

Page 20

A loophole... I had already left school. My family couldn't afford university fees. I worked in an office during the day and attended night school in the evening, living alone in a small attic room in a corner of Shanghai.

I skipped my specially chosen Japanese class and took a tram to Avenue Joffre. It was 8:30 PM. She was sitting there waiting for me. We chose a corner in the cinema. "The one who's aggressively pursuing you?" I asked. She shook her head. "It's too tiring!" "So you need to be in love." She gently tapped the back of my hand. "Love Tragedy" appeared in the darkness.

"Where to?" I asked as we walked closely along Avenue Joffre after watching Greta Garbo die in the film. "It's early." We talked, walked, and laughed until we arrived at my home. We kissed in the attic room. At 2:00 AM, she showed no sign of leaving. "Won't your cousin be sleeping late?" "She's already dreaming." "Then you should go back to school?" "I took two days off, saying I was going home." She replied, her face flushed. "×Na, no!" I grabbed her arms, stared at her, and remained silent for a long time. Finally, I quietly sent her back to school. The next evening, I received a letter from her. She confessed, she asked for my forgiveness... The love continued... I fell ill, spending three months in a third-class hospital ward. I returned to my hometown, a desolate temple-like house. I was sick for a year. I received two letters from her, one-fiftieth of the number I sent.

I returned to Shanghai and went to her school. She told me she was engaged to the man in the Western suit. She got married and became a mother of one... Seven years, eight years... "She came back yesterday. I haven't seen her," I replied to my eldest cousin, hurriedly walking out. My eldest cousin's sigh followed me. Garbo's car sped toward a tree, crashing loudly, shattering to pieces, both person and car. (From "Love Tragedy") A shadow flashed across my mind, seven or eight years ago!

Humor in Advertisements 281

— Hu Chen

"If you cannot dominate the field of love in life, you should also leave a fragrant name on the battlefield in death" - An advertisement for "Serving the Country with Glory" - Ling He has already given an appropriate critique of the film "Serving the Country with Glory." It is a film of a speculative nature, and this spirit is also infused into the advertisement - This is the shamelessness and sin of the declining intellectuals! This is completely pandering to the general muddle-headed youth who like to show off, with such muddle-headed things.

According to this advertisement, it seems that as long as one can dominate the field of love in life, there is no need to die on the battlefield; dying on the battlefield is because one cannot dominate the field of love. Therefore, dying on the battlefield is not the motive for serving the country with glory, but dominating the field of love is the motive for serving the country with glory. This fully demonstrates the shameful ignorance of the shameful intellectuals - Does this not completely demonstrate the ignorance of the leisured class towards the concept of the nation? What is the nation? Answer me!

Here, we should not think that it is one person's mistake. There are many, many of me, the entire leisured class, completely has such a mistake - a blindness to the two words "nation."

And this person exposed this ignorance on behalf of these people because he reflected this social consciousness. The two words "nation" are an empty concept. We must understand what its essence is - why should we strive for its glory instead of striving for our own?

Only after understanding what the essence of this nation is can we talk about everything else.

And what we are striving for is "glory." Is it "benefit"? - If we strive for glory but lose our own benefit, it is better not to strive for glory. - If we strive for our own benefit but lose empty glory, benefit is better. We should not strive for empty glory, but for our own real benefit!

I conclude that this advertisement is a humorous advertisement. It is made to satirize the members of the leisured class.

Amateur Mailbox

The Life of a Family 282

— Chen Guanhua

Dear Editor: It is truly shameful to say that I am already twenty years old and will soon be a high school graduate! However, regarding my own affairs - family problems, or rather, the crisis of my future - I have thought about it again and again, but I have never come up with a solution.

Now, I have decided to tell Mr. Editor in detail about my family situation and problems...

(1) Source of Income - My grandfather was originally a very poor private school teacher. Fortunately, my father had some intelligence and talent, and twenty years ago, he made a mess of teaching and being a politician (not very much), and got some money and wealth (not much), so I was able to go to school from a young age. His current occupation is different from before. In the countryside, he is both a gentleman and employs workers to till the fields, and he also has two small shops in small market towns outside. Originally, there were three shops in total in the early years, but due to the bankruptcy of the countryside and the decline of commerce in recent years, the larger one in the city closed down at the end of last year!

(2) Family Situation - The lives of my family of more than ten people (including two orphaned sons of my deceased uncle and several workers and maids) are all supported by the above-mentioned occupations, and the above-mentioned occupations must be maintained by my father alone. I have six brothers and three sisters in total. My mother only gave birth to me and two older sisters (already married). The only male child is me. The other five younger brothers and one younger sister (all unmarried, now four younger brothers and my younger sister are all studying) were all born to my stepmother. By the orders of my parents and the urging of relatives, I got married when I was seventeen years old after graduating from junior high school, and I already have children! Since the Republic of China, until the year before last, although my mother would sometimes quarrel with my stepmother, they always cared about their reputation and no major violent incidents occurred. It can be said that they "lived in peace."

(3) The Occurrence of the Problem - It was around March or April of last year, my father took a fancy to a maid in his own home, so he took her as his third concubine. After that, her mother often came to my house to make trouble. If her mother only wanted some money to use, my father could have given it to her because he loved her daughter. However, she wanted to make an agreement with my mother - to have me and my younger siblings call her daughter "Mom," etc. - such indecent conditions, how could my mother and stepmother be willing to obey her? So they made trouble, making a complete mess. Under this circumstance, if my father could handle it properly, the problem would not have escalated. However, my father was both infatuated with the maid and had no way to deal with her mother. All the disputes were blamed on my old mother. Therefore, my old mother developed the thought of being tired of the world.

(4) Hopelessness of Resolution - I know that my father's behavior, although "taking a maid as a concubine" is acceptable in popular customs, in law, he has committed the crime of raping a young girl under Article ?. Therefore, in order to make my father change his ways, and also for the sake of my family's reputation and my academic future, etc., I once wrote many letters to persuade my father, and also wrote letters to persuade my mother and asked my wife to persuade my mother not to pay attention to all their rights and wrongs, and let my father do as he pleases. However, my father did not accept my advice and was still confused and muddle-headed, and my wife was stupid and did not know how to mediate from it, and my mother was even more unable to bear it and often argued with the maid's mother and my father.

(5) Future Crisis - Mr. Editor, you think how dangerous this phenomenon is! Originally, according to my personal strange views, copper coins are hateful things, and the legacy of my father's industry is especially not worth cherishing. Secondly, my father's behavior - polygamy, indulging in lust - should be eradicated, whether for the sake of customs or for the sake of society. However, he has also done a lot of good for society - the lives of my family of more than ten people all depend on him, and the studies of my brothers all depend on him. If he is accused of his crimes (the mediocre maid, although she is now under my father's lustful power and has not shown any resistance. But her mother's greed, and her future conduct, cannot be changed), and he is imprisoned or goes bankrupt, wouldn't the lives of my family be ruined? Mr. Editor, you pity my young siblings and my old mother, and my ability is not enough to bear such a great responsibility!

(6) Several Questions - I now want to ask Mr. Editor to come up with a few methods. How can the maid's mother be prevented from coming to my house to quarrel with my mother in the future (it must be known that my father's small amount of material wealth cannot fill her endless greedy sea!)? If she comes to my house to ask for money or things, what attitude should my mother and my brothers and wife take? How can we prevent or avoid the maid's mother from accusing my father of his crimes? How can my father's crimes be mitigated? My father's crime - if she accuses him of raping a young girl (I am not very clear whether the maid's age is eighteen or seventeen) or other crimes - what is the highest and lowest sentence he should be imprisoned for? And is there a possibility of bankruptcy? If my father is imprisoned or goes bankrupt, what should I do and what ways can I maintain the lives of my family of more than ten people?

I hope that Mr. Editor, no matter how busy you are with work, please take some time to think of a solution for me! And I hope that Mr. Editor will think from my position and environment! I am now waiting for Mr. Editor to reply in the "Amateur Mailbox" of your esteemed newspaper or directly, and I will not only thank you in my heart, but also wish you well! Your follower Chen Guanhua

(The reply will be continued tomorrow)

He has experience with various machines and can also drive a car. He is now willing to work as an employee at a domestic or foreign automobile company or on a long-distance highway. Salary is not an issue. Mailing address: c/o Mr. Bing, No. 8 Hua'an Lane, Xujiahui Road, this city. Mr. Yin Wudu, from Wujin, is 34 years old and skilled in carpentry and painting. He is now willing to take on decoration work at organizations, foreign firms, or universities. Those who wish to hire him can write to No. 16 Zhiyang Lane, Huishan Road, Jingzhou Road Intersection.

Novel

Lulu's Victory (10) 283

— Written by Italian M. Celao, Translated by Jing Xin

Sophia's voice was solemn and resonant. Robert listened with great joy, as if he were hearing it for the first time. He felt as if he were facing a woman he had never met before. Her every word and every expression revealed her unique personality. Sophia had lost her cold appearance. She even looked at him, smiled, and talked to him as if he were a friend. How had they been before? What were they like now?

"When I like a book," Robert continued, "I always want to know the author very much, to know if he (or she) is kind, if he has suffered, if he has suffered, if he has ever loved -" "Perhaps you will be disillusioned. Writers always depict the love of others, but do not write about their own."

"Probably because they are concerned." "I think it is because of jealousy. In many cases, love is the only treasure hidden in the soul." But when Sophia said these words, her voice did not change. Her face showed such a frank expression, and her tone was so simple, so pure, so sincere, that Robert was not surprised to hear her talk about love so frankly. Nothing surprised him now. Everything seemed natural, expected. Even being alone with this strange daughter tonight seemed destined and long awaited. When they parted, they stared at each other face to face, as if hoping to confirm their renewed acquaintance. Sophia extended her hand, Robert took it, and bowed over it. A curtain fell heavily behind him. They parted.

After the charm of Sophia's face and speech disappeared, Robert felt confused, his head spinning. They were both joyful and melancholic, wanting to die, and yet full of vitality. He didn't know how to think about Lulu, about himself, about his future.

Sophia was very happy, very happy. For this reason, she cried, sobbing painfully, her head buried in her pillow.

Three months passed, and Lulu's wedding was still postponed. Her mother, who did not understand the reason for the postponement, often called her daughter aside and asked her for the reason.

Movie Special

Roosevelt's Movie Revival Movement 284

— Ji Yang

Since the Democratic Party came to power in the United States and took control of the government of the United States of America, it has been frantically implementing the Blue Eagle Movement - that is, the American Revival Movement.

Roosevelt provided relief to agriculture and industry and proposed the "Agricultural Act" and the "Emergency Plan." He dreamed of rescuing the United States from the flood of total collapse. Therefore, he also stipulated a "revival plan" for the film industry, one of the five major industries in the United States. Because, from 1932 to 1933, the American film industry experienced an "economic depression year" that was historically unprecedented. "Paramount Pictures," whose deficit reached as high as 30 million gold yuan, was almost bankrupt by January of this year. The rest, such as Warner Brothers, Fox, etc., all encountered an unprecedented economic panic. By the spring of this year, Roosevelt's expansion policy was effectively implemented, and like the general business community, the film industry also enjoyed a little bit of an optimistic atmosphere like the Indian summer of October. However, whether it can actually reverse the film industry's panic cannot be said today. What is seen is only Will Hayes's brain-wracking new control plan.

Will Hayes is the authority in the American film industry. He recently made five recommendations to the M.P.P.D.A. (abbreviation for Motion Picture Producers and Distributors of America, the representative body of the American film industry, whose president is Will Hayes).

1. Return movie theaters to their old owners. Two thousand movie theaters went bankrupt in the past year. The reduction in the number of viewers is endless, and the rational control of screenings is essential.

2. Regional distribution contracts. If this plan is implemented, it can save 6 million gold yuan in unnecessary expenses each year. In order to unify affairs, film storage warehouses must be established in various regions.

3. Savings in production costs. This is always necessary, especially at this time. It must be thoroughly implemented as the basis for rationalization. Salary reductions for actors are useless as a partial makeshift policy.

4. Consolidate necessary franchise rights in film production. From the sound recording of sound films to general technology, original works, etc., the rationalization of organization can save production costs.

5. Film purification movement. Just as international coordination diplomacy is the mask of imperialism, gentlemen's agreements must be concluded between producers on the surface, thereby achieving the control of large capital monopoly.

Will Hayes racked his brains and came up with this control method for the American film industry, which was bankrupt again and again. He injected a life-saving injection for the American film industry. He became the "only loyal subject" of Roosevelt's movie revival movement. But can this film rationalization plan achieve some degree of effect?

Needless to say, the economic depression in the American film industry is not so simple that it can be reversed by this control. Because it is one of the large enterprises, it must sensitively reflect the general trends of the capitalist economy, and at the same time, it cannot be immune to the changes in the world financial market at all times.

Therefore, whether Roosevelt's movie revival movement can revive the American film industry, I am afraid that even Roosevelt himself is not sure now!

Movie Review

Review of "Isle of Paradise" 285

— Ling He

Isle of Paradise - Jincheng -

Regarding documentary films of local customs and cultures, there is undoubtedly great value in science. However, it must be explained in detail here that a documentary film is by no means a purely objective transfer of things from a certain place to the screen unconditionally. On the contrary, it must pass through the subjective views of the author and be filmed after the author's own thinking and selection. Therefore, documentary films still represent the author's thoughts and belong to his own class, becoming something that is beneficial to this class. Obviously, the author of "Isle of Paradise" tried his best to adopt the lives and simple human feelings of the people of that small island. This is to say that that place is a paradise on earth, and the workers of the Dutch are living and working in peace and contentment, without any worries. Moreover, the Dutch authorities have tried to improve agriculture or fishery with machines, but the natives do not comply. At the same time, the Dutch government is also doing its best to improve superstitions, etc. All of these attempt to explain that the Dutch government is very kind to the natives, but the so-called barbaric workers are too stubborn.

Here, is it not enough to prove the author's intentions? The Dutch island is already "Isle of Paradise." Please let imperialism rule the world, because we can live and work in peace. Although I have not been to Southeast Asia, I believe that the people under the rule of imperialism are definitely not so pure and kind.

Movies have become a weapon of resistance, but they are also a tool of rule. Of course, documentary films are no exception.

There is another issue that is worth raising here, and that is whether documentary films also need the interspersion of stories?

When I walked out of the Jincheng Grand Theater, I heard many people say, "It doesn't make any sense." This is by no means accidental. Even at the time of the screening, many people left the venue. This is because they could not stand such a dull atmosphere. They are not used to movies without a story, because in people's habits, they come to see the bizarre and tortuous stories.

Of course, this is a problem of the audience's cultural level. Most of them are unwilling to treat the cinema as a classroom. We have not forgotten the lessons learned when "Spring Silkworms" was screened. Then, in order to make up for the shortcomings of this transitional era, I think it is still necessary to construct a simple story in documentary films. This is to say that we must increase the audience's interest in the picture.

However, we are in principle opposed to adding stories to documentary films, because that will lose the true value of introduction and record. However, under the conditions that do not harm the record of local customs, why not intersperse everything that we should record in the story? "Eskimo" gave us an excellent example. - The above, I hope to attract the attention of readers.

Speaking of this film, I think the photography skills, framing methods, and picture montage are very commendable. If you are a group of people who want to know the local customs and cultures of Southeast Asia, this is undoubtedly a very valuable film.

Three Questions That Scared Little Van Dyke 286

— Response

Not long ago, Little Van Dyke returned to Hollywood from London, preparing to produce a "Success Story." He arrived by plane. At the airport, many journalists were waiting for him. As soon as his foot touched the ground, he was surrounded by the journalists. Everyone knows that American journalists like to be direct and unceremonious. So, one reporter began to ask, "I heard that your father is about to marry Lady Ashworth. Do you like it or not?" Little Van Dyke was momentarily stunned, not knowing how to respond. Afterward, he told his friend that he wished he could punch that journalist in the nose, but she was a female reporter, so he couldn't be too reckless. So, he could only touch his cheek and pretend to ponder, "Lady Ashworth... let me think... the name is familiar, but I can't quite remember." (Presumably, readers will remember that this Lady Ashworth is old Van Dyke's lover. Her husband has already filed for divorce in court, accusing old Van Dyke of adultery. This news has been published in newspapers at home and abroad not long ago.)

Before he could dodge one bullet, another one came. The second question was, "Are you willing to let Joan Crawford marry Francbot Lone?" This was simply outrageous. So, without waiting for the third shot, he ran away. The third question, it is said, was, "When are you going to marry Gertrude Lawrence?" Gertrude is a London actress. She is already thirty-five years old, while Little Van Dyke is only twenty-six years old. It is said that they are deeply in love and do not mind the age difference. But according to news from London, Gertrude herself has denied the matter. However, in terms of age, it is not strange for the wife to be older than the husband. Among Hollywood stars, Swanson is older than Fairbairn, and Clark Gable's wife is also older than him, so it's not surprising.

Katherine Hepburn's Husband 287

— Fulun

Not long ago, this publication published a piece saying that American actress Katherine Hepburn imitated Greta Garbo's eccentricity, deliberately being vague about everything about herself, making people suspicious. Some people say she's been married and has two children, and she says, "Isn't that right, I have two children, one as white as snow, and one as black as pitch!" After she said that, she laughed non-stop. Do you believe her or not? Now, it has been confirmed that she has been married before. Katherine's husband's name is Ludlow Smith, a broker for an insurance company in New York. They have been married for three years. Presumably, from now on, Katherine won't deny it again!

Tianyi Tells You 288

— Liang Yu

(1) "Red Chamber Spring Depths" started filming the day before yesterday. The film is written by Cao Xuesong, directed by the bearded Gao Lihen, and stars Chen Yumei. (2) The new photography studio is currently under construction with doubled efforts. It is expected that it will be completed in another week. The company authorities added two new-style cameras yesterday, as well as a large number of mercury lamps and giant light bulbs, for use in the new photography studio. (3) Wang Cilong's "Two Brothers From" was completed earlier. However, during the screening the other day, Wang Cilong felt that the outdoor shots needed to be reshot, so he led the staff to the Bund yesterday morning to reshoot the morning scenery on the river. (4) During the screening of "Red Powder Iron Blood" the other day, all those who participated in the screening praised it unanimously, believing it to be a super-special work by Wang Yuanlong. (5) "Spring Night Song" filmed a dance hall scene last night. The dance hall scene was huge, occupying seven-tenths of the entire photography studio, and was designed by artist Xu Xingzhi. More than a hundred male and female extras were hired during the filming, acting as dancers and dance hostesses. The female lead, Ye Qiuxin, wore Western-style attire, with jade arms and fair wrists, and was extremely beautiful. (6) "Songstress's Scandalous History" has been completed and is now being edited and will soon be sent to Beijing for review. (Respectfully submitted)

"Blaze" Passes Censorship 289

The film "Blaze," directed by Hu Rui and starring Peng Fei and Hu Ping, produced by Yihua Film Company, has been in production for several months, sacrificing a lot of money and effort. It was just completed last month. In the film, the strongman Peng Fei performs in a fire pit, which is very thrilling, and Hu Ping lying on her back in the raging fire also makes people's souls fly to the ninth heaven. Now "Blaze" has been completely passed by the Nanjing Film Review Board. Once the sound dubbing is completed, it will be publicly screened at the highest-level theater in Shanghai.

Movie Novel

Romantic History of Mount Hua (3) 290

— Xin Chun

Soon after, the revolutionary army quickly occupied Shanghai. The Shanghai Alumni Association of Jinghua University, initiated by Hong Jiachen and others, held a welcome party for their old classmate, Chen Beifeng, a revolutionary comrade who had fought hard in Hunan and Hubei.

At the welcome party, Beifeng met old friends and also met Jiachen and Yulan, who had caused him to suffer a crushing defeat in love. Everyone warmly welcomed him. He looked down at the bright red corsage and suddenly remembered the blood on Huang Zhensheng's chest when he died in battle, which made him feel lost.

Jiachen and Yulan greeted Beifeng warmly, but it also made Beifeng feel a little sad. Yulan stared at him and said happily, "Beifeng, I haven't seen you in three years, and you are already a revolutionary hero!"

"You are a modern, beautiful lady!" Beifeng replied. Jiachen said beside him, "Alas! Time has changed us all."

Indeed, time has changed them! Beifeng has become a soldier with a face full of dust and deep melancholy, while Jiachen is already a young gentleman, and Yulan is a charming and romantic modern young woman.

The wine, the green lights, and the noisy laughter of the classmates could not arouse Beifeng's interest. When the banquet was over, someone saw Beifeng's melancholy and stood up to suggest to everyone, "We should make the most of this rare opportunity to have some recreational activities..." This suggestion was approved by everyone, and he turned his head and pointed to Beifeng and said, "Classmates, you won't forget Beifeng's music, will you? Now I propose... please Brother Beifeng play a song here!"

Beifeng declined, but when he saw Yulan clapping, he pondered for a moment, as if something was driving him, and immediately agreed.

Playing the old tune again, Beifeng's face was full of sadness. This color then infected Yulan's face, and she lowered her head and also became melancholy because of the piano sound. Jiachen was also pondering beside him.

Amid the firecracker-like applause, Beifeng finished playing, and when he stood up to salute the crowd, he was also filled with sadness, and tears almost welled up in his eyes.

Because of the感慨 of the vicissitudes of life and because of the unexpected impact of the environment, Beifeng became passive again.

One lonely morning, when Yulan was washing up, the maid brought in a letter from Beifeng. After she read the letter, her face suddenly turned a terrible gray. She hurriedly got into a car and rushed to the hotel where Beifeng was staying. The porter told her, "Mr. Chen has already returned to the headquarters early in the morning." She ran to the headquarters again, and the adjutant said to her, "Captain Chen has already left on the early train. I heard he went to Mount Hua." (To be continued)
